- Universal fix: Dependency states retain their exact dependency identities and nondependency capacity, while equivalent states are compared by the same educational dominance order used at final selection: released slots, roots, organizer-preserved exact witness, organizer retention, then stable reel order. Plain candidates are folded through a bounded semantic-mask DP after the dependency frontier, preventing root-depth history from overriding a better remediation set.
- Focused retest: The easy-exact plus joint-witness counterexample displaces the unnecessary wrapper. A 12,000-case brute-force audit, including full and partial dependency DAGs and 7,829 cases where a semantic root can add no new nondependency reel, found zero primary or organizer-semantic mismatches.

### AF-137 — Linear exact-difficulty feasibility search can violate release latency

- Status: Fixed locally; repeated sub-second guards passed; exact new-SHA latency retest pending
- Severity: Critical — mandatory postselection runs synchronously before the authoritative final event and can add seconds without any provider or database delay
- Reproduction: A legal 128-candidate, sixteen-obligation, nine-reel matrix with 34 exact candidates carrying distinct prerequisite subsets took 6.037 CPU seconds. Only the standalone exact candidate plus eight pair witnesses can complete the lesson.
- Root cause: Complete-cover selection reruns the set-cover search once for every infeasible exact-difficulty threshold, making runtime scale linearly with the number of exact alternatives.
- Universal fix: Complete-cover search branches on exact remediation first in increasing difficulty and proves the easiest feasible witness in one exhaustive pass. Selected-slot and root limits use cached monotonic searches, a safe remaining-capacity bound prunes impossible branches, and a cardinality-lower-bound probe skips the dense semantic frontier only when feasibility at that proven minimum is established. No provider call, wait, or healthy-path retry was added.
- Focused retest: The 128-candidate exact/dependency matrix repeatedly releases the standalone easiest feasible exact clip plus all sixteen facets in nine reels below the one-CPU-second guard. The no-exact and unavailable-facet guards also pass repeatedly; the full 69-test lesson-ordering suite passes.

### AF-138 — An unavailable exact-remediation closure can crash mandatory selection

- Status: Fixed locally; unavailable-exact regression and property audit passed; exact new-SHA adaptation retest pending
- Severity: Critical — a valid batch can fail before release when the only exact confusing/wrong-concept clip needs more prerequisite slots than the current release limit
- Reproduction: With a one-reel limit, the exact remediation requires one prerequisite and is therefore ineligible, while a standalone obligation witness remains eligible. The dependency-free solver indexes an empty exact-difficulty list and raises `IndexError`.
- Root cause: Exact availability is derived from all candidate reels, but optimizer difficulty thresholds are derived only from capacity-eligible closures; the empty intersection was not represented.
- Universal fix: The required exact bit and difficulty thresholds are derived only from capacity-eligible options. If no exact closure fits, exact remediation is marked unavailable for this release while the optimizer still maximizes every available grounded obligation; no family-level or lexical substitute is fabricated.
- Focused retest: The one-reel counterexample now releases its available obligation witness without an exception. The exhaustive audit covered 556 unavailable-exact cases and 1,376 unavailable obligation bits with no objective mismatch.

### AF-139 — Incomplete dependency-bearing coverage can exhaust the semantic state space

- Status: Fixed locally; sustained-suite and isolated latency guards passed; exact new-SHA latency retest pending
- Severity: Critical — one unavailable requested facet can add many seconds synchronously before the authoritative final event
- Reproduction: A 53-candidate batch with sixteen obligations, one deliberately ineligible ten-reel facet closure, one dependency-bearing witness, and forty 4-of-15 witnesses took 6.436 CPU seconds at a nine-reel release limit; a 73-candidate variant took 17.178 seconds.
- Root cause: Once complete cover is impossible, the dependency-state DP exhaustively explores through every root depth to prove maximal partial coverage and tie quality after the earlier unsafe early stop was removed.
- Universal fix: When complete cover is impossible, dependency-bearing options are explored only across semantic coverage, dependency identity, and nondependency capacity; dependency-free options are then folded through a 0/1 mask DP. Exact difficulty uses cached monotonic solves, and equivalent masks retain the educationally dominant representative without enumerating root histories. The semantic full-cover frontier remains a correctness fallback only when the cheaper cardinality-bound feasibility proof fails.
- Focused retest: The 53-candidate unavailable-facet matrix proves fourteen available facets are maximal and remains below the one-CPU-second guard under isolated and sustained-suite runs. The dependency/full-cover and dense dependency-free controls pass, and 12,000 exhaustive small cases show zero primary or organizer-semantic mismatches.

### AF-140 — First feasible complete cover can lose organizer-retention ties

- Status: Fixed locally; focused ties, expanded semantic oracle, and latency guards passed; exact new-SHA progression retest pending
- Severity: Medium — two equally complete, equally easy, equally sized lessons can choose a non-organizer clip instead of the organizer's intended clip
- Reproduction: At a two-reel limit, one exact `0.2` clip covers facets 0–3. Facet 4 can be completed either by an organizer-selected nonexact clip or a non-organizer exact clip. Both covers tie through exact presence, all five facets, difficulty, released slots, and roots, but the search returns the non-organizer pair.
- Root cause: Complete-cover feasibility returns the first solution at the proven difficulty/slot/root limits. Per-option branch ordering cannot guarantee the lexicographic organizer-retention and stable-ID tie of the combined selected set.
- Universal fix: After exact difficulty, released-slot count, and root count are proven, bounded feasibility passes first require an organizer-selected exact witness when one can participate in a complete cover, then search descending organizer-retention counts. Constrained states retain organizer identities so memoization cannot collapse a better organizer set. The ordinary dense path stops immediately when its first solution already reaches the provable organizer upper bound; no exhaustive terminal-history walk is added.
- Focused retest: Both the two-reel organizer-count tie and the dependency-bearing organizer-exact tie now retain the organizer's intended exact/companion clips. The 12,000-case oracle found zero primary or organizer-semantic mismatches, and repeated maximum-contract CPU guards pass at 0.56, 0.44, and 0.08 seconds. Exact deployed progression remains pending.

### AF-141 — First-hit partial mask DP can lose organizer-retention ties

- Status: Fixed locally; exact regression, lesson-ordering suite, and exhaustive semantic audit passed; exact new-SHA progression retest pending
- Severity: Medium — when not every requested facet fits, an equally complete partial lesson can discard two organizer-selected clips for a non-organizer alternative
- Reproduction: With three facets and a two-reel limit, two exact/nonexact pairs each cover the maximal two facets at the same exact difficulty and size. The first-hit DP returns a pair retaining one organizer clip although the other pair retains both.
- Root cause: The dependency-free mask DP keeps the first witness for each next mask and immediately returns the first state reaching the coverage upper bound. Neither step compares equal-primary-rank states using organizer retention and stable reel order.
- Universal fix: Each next-mask state now retains the full-rank dominant representative. A depth is evaluated completely, and only then does the solver return the best qualifying state; the earliest qualifying depth still proves minimum released slots and roots without reopening later-depth histories.
- Focused retest: The exact three-facet/two-reel organizer tie now retains both organizer choices. The 69-test lesson-ordering suite, 12,000-case semantic oracle, and all maximum-contract latency guards pass; exact deployed progression remains pending.

### AF-142 — Option compression can discard a globally preferable organizer exact clip

- Status: Fixed locally; exact compression regression, expanded semantic oracle, and latency guards passed; exact new-SHA progression retest pending
- Severity: Medium — the final complete lesson can use a non-organizer exact clip even though an organizer-selected exact clip preserves the same global remediation difficulty, coverage, and release capacity
- Reproduction: One `0.1` exact clip supplies facet 0. Two singleton exact clips supply facets 1–2: non-organizer difficulty `0.1` and organizer difficulty `0.2`. Once the first clip fixes global exact difficulty at `0.1`, either second clip ties on every primary objective, but pre-search compression keeps only the standalone-easier non-organizer option.
- Root cause: Option compression keys semantic mask, dependency identity, and capacity, then chooses by standalone selection quality. It omits organizer identity, whose contribution depends on which other clips are already selected and therefore cannot be safely reduced to standalone difficulty.
- Universal fix: The compression signature now includes the complete organizer-selected identity bitset in each closure. Semantically/capacity-equivalent non-organizer alternatives remain compressed, while distinct organizer contributions survive for the bounded organizer-exact/count feasibility passes.
- Focused retest: The two-reel exact reproducer now selects the `0.1` foundation plus the `0.2` organizer exact witness, not the semantically identical non-organizer alternative. The 12,000-case oracle found zero primary or organizer-semantic mismatches, and all three maximum-contract latency guards pass. Forty-seven index-only ties selected educationally and organizer-equivalent IDs and are non-semantic; deployed progression remains pending.

### AF-143 — Empty-topic joint intent can reference an unknown constraint and crash validation

- Status: Fixed locally; focused schema/retry and full selector-contract suite passed; exact new-SHA generation retest pending
- Severity: High — an otherwise schema-valid Gemini selector response can raise `KeyError` instead of producing a typed contract rejection that the selector step can retry
- Reproduction: For unfiltered URL/source generation (`topic=""`), return a request intent whose joint structure names a member or relation ID absent from its constraints. Nonempty topics reject this semantically, but the empty-topic path builds joint signatures by direct dictionary indexing and crashes.
- Root cause: `_RequestIntent` validates unique constraint and joint IDs but not referential integrity. The live empty-topic path intentionally skips request-grounding validation, leaving the unknown reference unguarded at signature construction.
- Universal fix: `_RequestIntent` model validation now enforces every joint member and relation ID against the same response's declared constraint-ID set. Invalid Gemini output therefore becomes the same typed schema rejection on filtered and unfiltered paths, preserving the selector's existing bounded retry behavior instead of reaching signature construction.
- Focused retest: Unknown member and unknown relation responses both fail model validation; the valid unfiltered synthetic-request control and repeated-invalid-schema retry control pass. The complete production selector-contract suite passes: 711 tests in 4.13 seconds.

### AF-144 — Local relationship keywords can override Gemini's semantic intent graph

- Status: Fixed locally; cross-domain selector regressions passed; exact new-SHA retest pending
- Severity: High — honest single concepts containing words such as `comparison` or `contrast` can be rejected repeatedly even though Gemini correctly returns one subject and no joint relationship
- Reproduction: `Explain the comparison principle in elliptic PDEs` and `Explain contrast dye in MRI` each return a grounded single SUBJECT with `joint_structures=[]`. Local request regexes classify both as multi-member comparisons and return `intent_contract_incomplete_joint_structure`.
- Root cause: The new explicit Gemini relationship graph remains gated by legacy prose classifiers that decide whether a graph must exist and whether a supplied relation span contains a locally recognized comparison marker. This duplicates semantic interpretation outside the AI contract.
- Universal fix: Local validation now checks only referential integrity, allowed relation roles, selected source-occurrence topology, and exact grounded evidence IDs for structures Gemini supplies. Whether the request contains a comparison, transition, or ordered relationship remains Gemini's semantic decision under the selector and independent-auditor prompts; no local relationship keyword decides that contract.
- Focused retest: Comparison-principle and contrast-dye single-concept controls pass without a graph. Biology, economics, AP Statistics, math, software, and law graph controls cover incident relationship nouns, multi-sentence/pronominal comparisons, adjacent definitions, invalid references/topology, and bounded retry behavior. Three stale direct-conversion regressions were reconciled with the AI-authority contract: graph fixtures now supply every AI-declared evidence ID, one deliberately reused AI-tagged quote is no longer locally reclassified, and plural/singular semantics no longer call the removed matcher. Live boundary regressions pass 20 tests, and the complete production selector-contract suite passes 731 tests in 3.74 seconds.

### AF-145 — Reordered repeated phrases can swap persisted obligation identity

- Status: Fixed locally; strict schema, dispatch-retry, and order-invariance regressions passed; exact new-SHA retest pending
- Severity: Critical — equivalent Gemini intent contracts can assign different durable concept-obligation keys to the same semantic requirement, breaking prior coverage and future thumb/quiz adaptation
- Reproduction: For `Teach C, then test C.`, constraints `[teach, test]` assign the first `C` span to teach and the second to test. Returning the identical constraints in `[test, teach]` order swaps those spans and therefore swaps the generated obligation keys.
- Root cause: Repeated exact source phrases were disambiguated by claiming the first unclaimed request span in constraint-list order, although the Gemini prompt declares constraint order irrelevant. The first fix added occurrence identity but left three universal holes: the semantic duplicate guard still case-folded `C` and `c`, Pydantic coerced booleans/floats/strings into integer occurrence indexes, and exact-request equality case-folded the user's copied request so a model could swap `C` and `c` before binding the occurrences.
- Universal fix: Every Gemini constraint now declares a strict nonnegative integer `source_occurrence`. Trusted conversion first compares the copied request with the shared semantic-token identity, which folds ordinary prose case but preserves structural case and compatibility math symbols, then resolves the numbered, mechanically grounded phrase occurrence to the exact case-preserving request slice and character offset before semantic deduplication; signature and persistence identity include that canonical position. Array order cannot assign spans, coercive types trigger the existing structured-response retry, and no local requirement-prose heuristic is used. Primary selector telemetry advances to `pro_boundary_v22`.
- Focused retest: Forward and reversed arrays produce identical live selector signatures and exact span/key mappings, including a leading multibyte emoji. Missing, repeated, out-of-range, boolean, float, and string occurrence claims fail closed; swapped structural-case and compatibility-symbol-collapsed requests are rejected before they can reverse the user's semantics, while harmless prose capitalization remains a healthy one-dispatch contract. A malformed first response dispatches exactly one immediate repair and recovers on its second dispatch; the healthy control dispatches once, and both paths prove there is no sleep. `Compare C and c.` retains two positioned members. The complete production selector-contract suite passes: 731 tests in 3.74 seconds.

### AF-146 — An exact reel ID can be re-released by a continuation batch

- Status: Fixed locally; exact-ID and full generation-job regressions passed; exact new-SHA retest pending
- Severity: High — the strongest possible duplicate can survive into a subsequent batch even though the parent reel was already authoritatively released
- Reproduction: An authoritative parent release contains `same-reel`; a child continuation returns another reel dictionary with `reel_id=same-reel`. The continuation temporal-overlap filter returns the child instead of removing it.
- Root cause: The overlap input de-duplicates `prior_reel_ids + current_ids` before filtering, then converts retained IDs to a set. The retained parent ID is therefore indistinguishable from permission to return the child dictionary with the same ID.
- Universal fix: Remove exact parent IDs from the current child-ID mapping before interval overlap evaluation. Preserve the old behavior for malformed reel dictionaries without IDs, and return an empty child batch when every valid child ID was already released.
- Focused retest: The exact parent/child ID regression, containing-span regression, bounded continuation-history query controls, organizer-prefilter capacity case, and all-overlap exhaustion case pass. The complete generation-job API suite passes: 189 tests in 2.51 seconds.

### AF-147 — Continuation overlap filtering occurs after organizer selection

- Status: Fixed locally; exact new-SHA full-suite and live continuation retests pending
- Severity: Critical — an already covered child clip can consume organizer capacity or satisfy a mandatory remediation/intent obligation, then disappear after ordering while a novel eligible alternative remains unselected
- Reproduction: A parent releases clip A. The child candidate pool contains same-source overlapping sibling B followed by novel alternative C. A capacity-limited organizer selects B; the post-order overlap filter deletes B and releases nothing, although C was available.
- Root cause: Fresh lesson ordering received the unfiltered continuation candidate pool. Temporal overlap removal was a release postcondition only, so Gemini and the mandatory-selection optimizer made decisions over candidates that could never surface.
- Universal fix: Filter prior-release exact IDs and temporal overlaps before computing the lesson-order prompt and mandatory postconditions. The organizer's output is then defensively intersected with that one surfaceable candidate snapshot without repeating database queries; stored-order replay retains its independent temporal filter.
- Focused retest: The tight parent-A/overlapping-B/novel-C regression now shows only C reaches the organizer and C is released. The larger bounded candidate-window, exact-ID duplicate, and containing-span controls pass together (4 tests in 2.77 seconds).

### AF-148 — The bounded organizer history can omit the only adaptive signal

- Status: Fixed locally; full optimizer and prompt-budget regressions passed; exact new-SHA and live thumb/quiz retests pending
- Severity: Critical — a thumbs-down or quiz-wrong concept can disappear from Gemini's organizer context solely because its stable concept key sorts after forty unrelated prior concepts
- Reproduction: Supply forty valid zero-signal prior concepts followed by a signaled prior concept whose family/title semantically matches a current candidate under a new concept ID. The old loop stops before computing its learner signal, so neither the adaptive signal nor its semantic bridge reaches the organizer.
- Root cause: `prior_concept_coverage` applies its forty-row cap in caller order before learner-signal lookup or candidate relevance. Main's coverage order is stable identity order, not adaptive importance.
- Universal fix: Normalize the complete bounded history first, then deterministically prioritize nonzero thumb/quiz signals, current candidate exact IDs, highest delivery frequency, and stable identity before retaining the existing forty-row/token cap. This changes no provider count or prompt-size ceiling.
- Focused retest: The 42-row regression retains the signaled old-ID semantic bridge first and the current exact-ID row second while remaining capped at forty. The full lesson-ordering suite passes: 69 tests in 1.77 seconds, including exhaustive semantic and latency guards.

### AF-149 — Case-sensitive one-letter concepts share adaptive history

- Status: Fixed locally; full shared-token/query/cache, exact new-SHA, and live C/c adaptation retests pending
- Severity: Critical — feedback or quiz mastery for one symbolic concept can suppress or amplify a distinct concept that differs only by meaningful case
- Reproduction: `normalize_clip_concept("C")` and `normalize_clip_concept("c")` produced the same normalized key. `ensure_clip_concept` therefore reused one concept ID/title, and thumbs or quiz outcomes leaked between the uppercase and lowercase identifiers even though positioned intent obligations distinguished them. The initial ASCII-only repair still merged Unicode mathematical pairs such as `Δ/δ`, while the selector's older case-folded semantic dedup rejected `Compare C and c.` before either concept could persist.
- Root cause: The shared structural-case tokenizer treated every one-letter alphabetic token as case-insensitive, and the selector independently repeated the same case-folded assumption before canonical request positions were available. That assumption is safe for prose articles/pronouns but false for identifiers, variables, matrix notation, genetics, programming symbols, and cased non-ASCII mathematical alphabets.
- Universal fix: The shared structural-case token rule now preserves any standalone single uppercase alphabetic Unicode token except ordinary one-letter prose stop words (`A` and `I`). The selector validates and canonicalizes each exact request occurrence before duplicate checking and includes the case-preserving text plus character offset in identity. Lowercase identifiers and ordinary title capitalization retain their prior behavior; attached language suffixes such as `C++` and `C#` retain their established normalization.
- Focused retest: C/c, X/x, and Δ/δ remain distinct; A/a and I/i remain equivalent; existing notation and suffix controls pass. `ensure_clip_concept` persists distinct C/c and Δ/δ IDs. Helpful-uppercase, confusing-lowercase, and wrong-quiz-lowercase signals remain isolated with adjustments `+0.04`, `-0.06`, then `-0.18` only for the lowercase concept. The shared token/adaptation matrix passes 37 tests in 0.68 seconds, and the upstream selector cases pass inside the 731-test contract suite.

### AF-150 — An all-overlap continuation can persist and activate an empty order

- Status: Fixed locally; full generation-job, exact new-SHA, and live continuation retests pending
- Severity: Critical — a continuation whose entire apparent inventory was already covered can persist `ordered_reel_ids=[]`, activate an empty generation, and prevent later inventory from receiving fresh adaptive ordering
- Reproduction: The outer release branch is entered because database inventory exists, but the new pre-organizer overlap filter removes every child candidate. The old flow still calls `order_lesson_batch([])`, writes empty v2 lesson metadata, and sets `activate_generation=True`.
- Root cause: Branch eligibility was computed before the surfaceability postcondition and was not reevaluated after overlap filtering.
- Universal fix: Materialize and prefilter the candidate pool before entering the ordering/release branch. An empty pool now uses the existing partial/exhausted path, performs no organizer call, writes no lesson order, and never activates the child; stored-order replay behavior is unchanged.
- Focused retest: The all-overlap worker regression ends exhausted with an empty authoritative payload, a failed non-activated child generation, no lesson-order metadata, and zero organizer/activation calls. It passes with the capacity, larger-window, and exact-ID continuation controls (4 tests in 1.84 seconds).

### AF-151 — The player can expose the first excluded neighbor cue at an exact end boundary

- Status: Fixed locally with focused and full-suite regressions; exact production replay pending the new deployed SHA
- Severity: Medium — a semantically complete clip can finish by flashing the next joke, aside, or sentence even though Gemini selected only educational cues
- Reproduction: Physics reel `ingest-1fbf62f103de41a1` correctly selects cues 6–16 and ends with “opposes motion, and is therefore to the left.” Its final range is exactly `44.079`, the recorded onset of excluded cue 17. At the player's `0:27 / 0:27` endpoint, YouTube displays cue 17's joke: “I feel like there should be snow on the ground.”
- Root cause: The timing contract records the excluded neighbor's onset as a legal inclusive final endpoint. The embed URL also rounds the end up to the next integer. YouTube pre-renders the newly active caption at that shared timestamp, so semantic exclusion alone does not prevent a visible endpoint leak.
- Universal fix: Treat a selected interval as half-open only when its final endpoint touches the grounded onset of the immediately excluded cue. The pipeline now moves that endpoint back by the existing 10 ms neighbor guard (matching the player's 10 ms poll/early-stop cadence), records the excluded-neighbor provenance, and applies the same guard to Gemini's playable fallback. Normal gaps, source-ending clips, intra-cue word projections, and materially overlapping authorized context remain unchanged; no text/topic heuristic was added.
- Focused retest: The exact `44.079 → excluded cue at 44.079` fixture persists `44.069`, retains the selected educational cue/text, and records the guard; normal-gap and same-cue projection controls remain unchanged, and Gemini fallback also returns `44.069`. The complete 162-test boundary/pipeline module and the clean staged-patch 2,845-test backend suite pass. Real player replay remains required on the new production SHA.

### AF-152 — Adaptive remediation searches the broad material request instead of the exact confusing concept

- Status: Fixed locally with deep/bootstrap retrieval and immutable-context regressions; exact production replay pending the new deployed SHA
- Severity: Critical — thumbs-down or quiz-wrong can spend a full provider batch on related material while returning no clip for the exact concept the learner missed
- Reproduction: “Need help” on `gravitational force components on an incline` correctly advanced feedback revision `1 → 2`, prioritized that exact acquisition concept, excluded the watched source, and launched a fresh job. The resulting Gemini selection contained `static vs kinetic friction` and `friction equations`, but zero clips with the confusing concept ID. The two-reel organizer batch therefore could not satisfy its exact-remediation invariant.
- Root cause: `generate_reels` selects the correct adaptive acquisition concept and passes its narrow title as `topic`, but passes the broad material `subject_tag` as `literal_topic` whenever the public request has no explicit `concept_id`. The production discovery path expands and searches `literal_topic`, so the narrow adaptive target is ignored while the stored `acquisition_concept_id` misleadingly remains correct.
- Universal fix: `discover_practice_fast` now expands and searches the narrow acquisition `topic` in both deep and bootstrap modes; `literal_topic` remains immutable request context for persistence/audit and can no longer overwrite retrieval. The non-Gemini selector fallback also uses the narrow acquisition topic while retaining the broad request in `_literal_topic` and `requested_topic`. No lexical or domain-specific matching was added.
- Focused retest: Differing Newton broad-request/narrow-concept fixtures prove that Gemini expansion, Supadata search, topic evidence, and selection all use the narrow focus while the broad request remains persisted. One healthy deep request still makes one expansion/search plan. The full 93-test practice-fast retrieval module and clean staged-patch 2,845-test backend suite pass. Physics, biology, math, software, and law feedback/quiz replay remains required on the new production SHA.

### AF-153 — A hard learner-level gate can release zero reels despite a complete relevant batch

- Status: Fixed locally with pipeline, legacy-row, worker-release, organizer, and full-suite regressions; exact production replay pending the new deployed SHA
- Severity: Critical — users see “Finding the first clips” and the worker spends another provider batch even though the first batch already contains relevant, self-contained, boundary-valid clips
- Reproduction: Beginner biology request `772e0703-0dc1-4834-a60e-18142b22c353` persisted five Gemini-selected clips covering the full requested progression (glycolysis, Krebs cycle, oxidative phosphorylation/oxygen, and ATP yield). Difficulties were `0.35–0.50`; all five were marked `surface_eligible=false, surface_reason=level_mismatch`. Generation `ef4f6525-aeea-4929-a27d-efa7ccb11b76` activated with five stored reels but emitted an authoritative empty final event, then launched another paid continuation while the UI remained empty.
- Root cause: The pipeline converts Gemini's numeric `difficulty` into a categorical hard surface gate before the lesson organizer sees the batch. Current-level counting excludes every deferred clip, ranked-feed filtering removes them again, and the worker mistakes a pedagogically rankable reservoir for zero usable reels. This creates two competing authorities: numeric difficulty/orchestrator progression versus a pre-organizer enum cutoff.
- Universal fix: Learner `knowledge_level` remains explicit and each clip retains only numeric `difficulty`; `deferred_level` is advisory metadata. Otherwise-valid clips are no longer converted to `surface_eligible=false`, legacy `level_mismatch` rows are treated as soft inventory, and cached hard-empty feed rows are invalidated. The organizer now receives the exact bands (`<0.34`, `0.34–<0.67`, `≥0.67`) and must prefer current band, then the closest adjacent band (easier first on a tie), then any valid coherent clip. Difficulty can never be the sole reason for an empty lesson.
- Focused retest: Current-band clips rank first; adjacent-band clips fill when current-band inventory is absent; all-above-band and legacy hard-gated batches release nonempty without another search; prerequisites remain ordered; changing learner level changes order but never membership. Lesson prompt/cache versions advance to `lesson_order_v10`/8 and ranked-feed cache to 47. The affected modules and clean staged-patch 2,845-test backend suite pass. Biology/math/software/law/advanced live controls and latency comparison remain required on the new production SHA.

### AF-154 — The apparent biology retry loop is already bounded to five fill attempts

- Status: Investigated on exact production SHA `e4f5bb918c686042617260dfd6f4511f42c445d8`; no separate defect or code change — the observed behavior is a consequence of AF-153
- Severity: Informational — repeated paid work is undesirable here, but the requested `3–5` cap already exists and the loop is not unbounded
- Evidence: Biology material `772e0703-0dc1-4834-a60e-18142b22c353` created initial job `6848ea7e-b719-423b-abe6-8c7900a9a045` followed by four zero-growth continuations, ending with job `9ebb65cb-665c-4106-b266-b81bcaa30716`. `bootstrapFirstReels` and `requestReadyBatch` cap a fill with `MAX_GENERATION_ATTEMPTS_PER_FILL=5` and `MAX_ZERO_GROWTH_CONTINUATIONS=3`; focused frontend tests already enforce both bounds. Provider steps independently use `max_attempts=3`.
- Decision: Preserve the existing universal caps. AF-153 will prevent valid level-deferred batches from entering this fallback at all; changing retry budgets would be unrelated to the actual root cause and could reduce recovery from genuinely empty provider batches.
- Retest required: After AF-153, the same biology request must release the first valid batch and create no zero-growth continuation. Existing five-attempt, three-zero-growth, recovery-after-progress, and authoritative-exhausted controls must remain green.

### AF-155 — A legacy dependent clip is still hard-gated by learner level

- Status: Fixed locally with pipeline, ranked-feed, cross-request, and three-level regressions; exact production replay pending the new deployed SHA
- Severity: High — an otherwise-valid dependent clip can disappear for a beginner even after its prerequisite is available, contradicting the rule that difficulty changes order but never membership
- Reproduction: A legacy beginner-compatible prerequisite persisted as `level_mismatch` and an advanced dependent persisted as `prerequisite_not_surfaceable` rank as only the prerequisite for a beginner. The same two rows rank as prerequisite then dependent after switching the learner to advanced.
- Root cause: Ranked-feed compatibility admits `prerequisite_not_surfaceable` rows to the dependency scheduler only when the dependent's numeric difficulty matches the learner's current band. The dependency scheduler already validates prerequisite availability, so this extra level predicate is a second hard gate.
- Universal fix: Admit legacy level-mismatch rows as otherwise-valid pipeline inventory and admit prerequisite-deferred rows to the existing dependency scheduler regardless of difficulty. Keep fail-closed prerequisite validation and let numeric difficulty affect only ordering.
- Focused retest: The same prerequisite/dependent pair remains available in dependency order for beginner, intermediate, and advanced learners; deleting the prerequisite hides the orphan. A real five-row legacy off-level source generation is reused across requests, all five candidates reach the organizer, and retrieval is never called. The affected 694-test matrix and clean staged-patch 2,845-test backend suite pass.

### AF-156 — Broad requests can produce umbrella clips containing several independent lessons

- Status: Fixed locally in the existing selector, Pro audit, and organizer paths; exact production replay pending the new deployed SHA
- Severity: High — a long candidate can begin before its named concept, include unrelated biography/jokes and several complete lesson stages, then duplicate shorter atomic candidates
- Reproduction: The live biology batch contained a 535-second umbrella spanning glycolysis, fermentation, Krebs, biography/jokes, electron transport, and ATP recap. A 439-second candidate labeled `electron transport chain` began during glycolysis; the actual ETC explanation started much later. Boundary diagnostics show Gemini authored the broad ranges and the local boundary layer preserved them.
- Root cause: The selector simultaneously requires one independently teachable objective and tells the PRIMARY clip to satisfy every request constraint in one contiguous span while wholeness outranks concision. For multi-part requests this rewards an umbrella PRIMARY. The existing audit cannot add/split clips, and organizer fallback can favor a lower-cardinality umbrella that covers more obligations.
- Universal fix: The selector now treats multi-part requests as curriculum coverage across atomic candidates, permits a broad overview only for a distinct taught integrative relationship, and preserves genuinely indivisible long derivations/problems. The existing Pro audit shrinks umbrella ranges to the nearest grounded atomic objective. The organizer prefers equivalent atomic coverage with less redundant watch time and never selects an umbrella with nested restatements; mandatory local reconciliation now preserves a complete dependency-safe AI selection instead of replacing it with a lower-cardinality umbrella. No fixed duration cap or extra model call is added.
- Focused retest: Physics, biology, math, software, and law prompt fixtures enforce atomic curricula; the Pro audit repairs an umbrella in its existing call; a complete three-clip cellular-respiration selection is not replaced by a 535-second umbrella; a unique 240-second indivisible derivation remains eligible. Selector contract (737), Pro output/call-budget (9), Gemini segment (636), lesson-ordering (71), affected matrix (694), and clean staged-patch backend (2,845) tests pass. Live cross-domain clip inspection remains required after deployment.

### AF-157 — An automatic fill batch can place a semantic near-duplicate immediately after an already released reel

- Status: Fixed locally after independent universality audit; the clean 2,866-test backend suite passes and exact production replay remains pending the new deployed SHA
- Severity: High — individually valid clips consume consecutive feed slots teaching the same learning objective, reducing coverage and making the lesson feel repetitive
- Reproduction: Fresh post-reset physics material `b7ea3c5b-35af-4f1c-a817-e794676cfc97` first released `ingest-70908851e9a24a79` (`free-body diagram of a stationary object`, 59.63 seconds). Its automatic fill then placed `ingest-b4f5c91c641d4bdd` (`balanced forces at rest`, 31.74 seconds) immediately next. Both independently draw the gravity/normal-force free-body diagram for an object at rest and conclude that balanced forces produce zero net force. The clips come from different videos and different generation batches, so exact-ID and same-source temporal-overlap guards do not catch them.
- Root cause: Exact-ID merge guards and temporal-overlap guards intentionally prove only exact/same-source duplicates. Cross-source equivalence belongs to the existing Gemini lesson editor, but `_lesson_prior_concept_coverage` gives it only prior concept IDs, broad family labels, titles, counts, and obligation keys. Candidate clips include summary/takeaway/transcript excerpts; already released clips do not. In this reproduction both clips even share the exact grounded request-obligation key, so mandatory coverage did not require the repeat—the editor lacked comparable prior teaching-objective content and selected every structurally valid candidate. The final merge then had no semantic evidence or authority to undo that AI choice.
- Universal fix: Each prior canonical concept now carries up to three distinct objectives from Gemini's compressed summary, using the grounded transcript only when that summary is absent. History is reconstructed in authoritative release order for every child generation, including feedback/quiz regenerations that have a source generation but no continuation token. The worker reuses the authoritative source-release snapshot already required by overlap filtering, falling back to continuation history only for legacy paths, so this coverage adds no query. The organizer receives its existing prioritized forty-concept lane plus a bounded newest-nine clip-level objective lane, so a relevant different-ID concept cannot disappear behind the concept cap. Normal and compact payloads preserve both lanes. The existing Gemini lesson editor compares that evidence with each current summary/takeaway/transcript and omits neutral cross-source/title/ID restatements unless a candidate adds a genuinely new explanation, reasoning step, application, misconception, remediation, or worked-example step. Lesson prompt/cache versions advance to `lesson_order_v12`/10.
- Independent clean-patch audit findings and correction: The first implementation measured the compact semantic ceiling from current candidates only, allowing distinct prior objectives to collapse to the same short prefix while leaving prompt budget unused. It could also let deterministic obligation coverage re-add a restatement Gemini intentionally omitted, a fixed forty-concept lane could discard the only relevant different-ID recent objective, and an identityless history row filtered out of the prompt could still authorize a declaration. The corrected compactor budgets current, canonical-prior, and recent-prior semantic evidence together and deduplicates after truncation; declaration validation trusts only prior evidence actually visible in the prompt. The same existing Gemini response now returns strictly validated, disjoint `prior_restatement_reel_ids`; only those omitted candidates' grounded obligation keys are exempt from reinsertion, while exact remediation still overrides the declaration and removes any re-added ID from it. Cache validation and persisted lesson metadata carry the same field. No embedding, lexical threshold, domain branch, duration rule, provider call, retry, wait, database round trip, or sleep was added.
- Focused retest: A domain-neutral prior balance explanation with a unique grounded obligation reaches one existing organizer call with no sleep; its cross-source paraphrase remains omitted while nonzero-response reasoning and a rotated-frame application remain in order. Source-generation history reaches Gemini identically with and without a continuation token and does not repeat the continuation-history lookup. Missing, unknown, duplicate, overlapping, evidence-free, canonical-prior, recent-prior-only, cached, mandatory-coverage, and remediation declarations are rejected or reconciled as specified. Multiple distinct objectives survive persistence, newest clip-level evidence crosses the forty-concept cap, and forced compact payloads share concept aliases, deduplicate after truncation, retain nonempty semantic evidence, and stay below 64,000 characters. Exact fresh physics replay remains required.

### AF-158 — Client reconciliation inserts a continuation delta ahead of the existing unseen lesson tail

- Status: Fixed locally with continuation/adaptive reconciliation regressions and the full frontend suite; exact production replay pending the new deployed SHA
- Severity: High — a background fill can reorder an already coherent lesson while the learner is watching it, place repeated foundations together, and move the original progression behind newly mined material
- Reproduction: The authoritative backend ancestry for fresh physics material `b7ea3c5b-35af-4f1c-a817-e794676cfc97` is the initial generation's seven ordered reels followed by the continuation generation's eight. When the continuation finalized, only initial reel 1 had durable watch progress. The client produced `[initial #1, continuation #1…#8, initial #2…#7]`, making the two stationary free-body examples adjacent even though the server chain separates them by six clips. No feedback or quiz state existed, so adaptive reranking did not justify the move.
- Root cause: `reconcileGeneratedReels` treats every later authoritative payload as a replacement tail: it places the incoming continuation rows immediately after the locked prefix and only then appends stable unseen rows from the current feed. A continuation payload is a delta that extends its source generation, not a replacement adaptive lesson, but the merge is not told which semantic it has.
- Universal fix: Reconciliation now receives explicit settlement semantics. A plain request carrying the server continuation token produces `locked prefix + stable unseen lesson + authoritative continuation delta`; page-one/durable-job continuation recovery uses the same append mode. Goal remediation and adaptive replacement retain the prior replacement mode, so feedback and quiz results can still place newly ranked material directly after the locked prefix. Identity deduplication is unchanged, and no request, poll, provider call, or wait was added.
- Focused retest: With one locked reel, two unseen original lesson steps, and a two-reel continuation delta, settlement preserves `locked + existing explanation + existing application + continuation reasoning + continuation example`. Runtime callback controls prove explicit append and replacement modes reach reconciliation; restored-inventory, rejected-provisional, watched-frontier, and focused-remediation replacement controls remain green. TypeScript and the production Next.js build pass. Exact browser replay remains required.

### AF-159 — The organizer can receive the selected level instead of the adjusted effective level

- Status: Fixed locally with submission/worker/prompt regressions; the clean backend suite passes and exact production adaptation replay remains pending
- Severity: High — feed ranking and Gemini lesson ordering can prefer different soft difficulty bands after thumbs or quiz evidence shifts the learner target
- Reproduction: An intermediate learner with a `+0.20` adaptive adjustment has an effective target of `0.70`, inside the advanced band. Ranking computes that adjusted target, but the durable generation job stores only `knowledge_level=intermediate`, so the organizer is told to prefer intermediate clips.
- Root cause: The API already loads learner progress and computes the effective numeric target for feed ranking, but does not persist that derived value in job request parameters. The background worker therefore has no consistent adjusted target to pass to the organizer and falls back to the base enum.
- Universal fix: Both direct generation and feed autofill persist the already-computed `effective_level_target` without another database query. The worker passes that 0..1 value alongside the selected base level. Gemini receives one continuous per-clip `difficulty` source of truth and the exact matching band boundaries; it uses the adjusted target's band first, the closest adjacent band next (easier first on a tie), and any relevant valid clip after that. A redundant clip-level enum is intentionally not added because it could disagree with the score and would consume semantic prompt budget. Legacy jobs safely fall back to the selected label. Generation request schema advances to `adaptive_clip_concepts_v5` so pre-fix stored orders cannot be reused. No provider call, retrieval, retry, database query, poll, wait, or sleep was added.
- Focused retest: A direct intermediate/+0.20 submission persists target `0.70`; the worker forwards both `learner_level=beginner` and a deliberately different effective target `0.70` unchanged; the prompt exposes that target and all existing current/adjacent/farther inventory-retention controls remain green. Live thumbs/quiz frequency, ordering, and TTFR comparison remain required on the exact deployed SHA.

### AF-160 — An unreleased source generation can fail while exporting organizer history

- Status: Fixed locally after the complete clean backend suite exposed the regression; focused and full-suite retests pass and exact production replay remains pending
- Severity: High — a durable child job can terminate instead of returning otherwise-valid clips when its source generation has no authoritative final event
- Reproduction: Ten existing worker controls created a source generation without an authoritative release and entered continuation overlap filtering. The clean suite failed with `TypeError: 'NoneType' object is not iterable` before ranking, so the jobs emitted only terminal failures.
- Root cause: The authoritative-release snapshot deliberately returns `None` to distinguish “no authoritative release exists” from an authoritative empty release. AF-157's new optional history export iterated that sentinel before the pre-existing no-history guard.
- Universal fix: Preserve the sentinel contract and return the candidate reels unchanged before exporting history whenever no authoritative source release exists. This changes neither provider work nor database access and leaves the output collector empty.
- Focused retest: A child with a real source-generation link but no authoritative final keeps its reel, exports no prior IDs, and does not throw. All 195 generation-job API controls and the complete 2,866-test backend suite pass.

### AF-161 — The singleflight organizer path renders the same prompt twice

- Status: Fixed locally after candidate/base comparison and profiling; focused latency, full backend, frontend, typecheck, and production-build retests pass
- Severity: High — redundant prompt compaction consumes avoidable CPU immediately before final clips can be released, and richer prior-objective evidence makes that duplicate work more expensive
- Reproduction: The 128-candidate maximum-obligation and dependency-constrained partial-cover controls intermittently exceeded their one-second CPU guard. The unchanged deployed-base checkout reproduced the same failures at up to 1.31 seconds and 1.06 seconds; profiling showed two identical calls through `_user_prompt` and `_bounded_user_prompt` for one organizer dispatch.
- Root cause: A cache miss acquires the lesson-order singleflight lock by recursively re-entering `_order_lesson_batch`. The recursive call revalidates the batch correctly, but also rebuilds the immutable prompt and cache key that the outer call just computed.
- Universal fix: Pass the already-rendered user prompt, cache key, and prior-evidence flag into the locked recursive call. Input-ID validation, cache recheck, exact-cover reconciliation, provider dispatch, retries, queries, waits, selected membership, and ordering semantics are unchanged.
- Focused retest: The maximum-obligation and unavailable-dependency controls pass below one CPU second while preserving full obligation coverage, remediation, dependency closure, the nine-reel ceiling, and deterministic order. The prompt/dispatch control observes one prompt render and one provider call. The final clean matrix is 2,866 backend tests plus 44 subtests, 186 frontend tests, TypeScript, and a Next.js production build.

### AF-162 — The deployed Gemini lesson organizer rejects valid candidate batches before applying semantic sequencing

- Status: Fixed locally; focused regression and exact corrected-contract provider probe pass, with deployment replay pending
- Severity: High — valid, relevant atomic candidates exist, but the organizer falls back before it can apply semantic duplicate removal, prerequisite ordering, adaptive signals, or the soft-level policy
- Reproduction: Fresh production material `e46ada2b-a4a0-434f-ae02-60c82a950a88` produced five valid stored Newton candidates. Both `lesson_order_v12` calls to `gemini-2.5-flash-lite` returned HTTP 400 in about one second with no response tokens. The deterministic fallback released a 476.43-second umbrella acceleration solution while omitting shorter atomic incline-diagram and gravity-component prerequisites; a later released tension clip refers to the prior acceleration result for context.
- Confirmed scope: This is not a retrieval or hard-level-filter failure: five valid candidates spanning difficulty `0.35` to `0.60` were persisted, and the deployed organizer prompt already requires current band, closest adjacent band, then any relevant valid clip. The failure occurs at the organizer provider contract before those semantic instructions run.
- Root cause: AF-157 added a third `maxItems: 200` array to the Pydantic JSON Schema sent to Gemini. An exact minimal production-key probe reproduced HTTP 400 `INVALID_ARGUMENT`: the schema constraint has too many serving states, with long array length limits called out by the provider. The same model and schema returned HTTP 200/`STOP` when only the three provider-side `maxItems` keywords were removed; the nullable `default`, 10,240-token ceiling, and disabled-thinking configuration were unchanged. Google documents this model as available and quota exhaustion as HTTP 429, so neither Tier 2 nor model availability caused this deterministic 400.
- Universal fix: Keep Pydantic's strict 200-item bounds for local response validation, but omit those grammar-expanding array ceilings only from the schema sent to Gemini and from the matching cache-contract hash. Required fields, types, `additionalProperties: false`, ordered-list nonemptiness, semantic validation, the two-attempt fallback policy, and every organizer instruction remain unchanged. The fix adds no provider call, retry, wait, or healthy-path latency; an unchanged deterministic 400 still fails fast instead of wasting a retry.
- Focused regression and exact retest: The request-config test proves the lean schema is the one dispatched. A dedicated control proves all three provider arrays omit `maxItems` while the local model still rejects 201 IDs. The exact production-key contract probe changes from HTTP 400 to HTTP 200/`STOP`. Full suites, exact-SHA deployment, and fresh live cross-domain/adaptation replay remain pending.

### AF-163 — A fast partial batch can stream an advanced requested constraint before later-retrieved foundations

- Status: Fixed locally with organizer, persistence, replay, feed-order, and active-reel race regressions; exact-SHA deployment replay pending
- Severity: High — each batch is coherent in isolation, but append-only continuation can make the complete lesson run application before concept and prerequisite steps
- Reproduction: Fresh production material `3f0b3a2b-6766-4f6c-b456-377e3bb38189` requested intuitive net force and free-body diagrams through `F=ma`, then two progressively harder problems including an incline. The first 68.64-second partial released a 58.96-second incline derivation and a 150.37-second incline problem. Its continuation later released nine non-degraded organizer selections beginning with Newton-law proportionality, force/acceleration direction, and a simple one-force calculation, followed by friction and atomic FBD steps. AF-158 correctly appends a plain continuation, so the visible global order is incline application/problem before the foundations requested first.
- Confirmed scope: Level filtering did not cause the gap: both generations retain beginner/intermediate candidates, and both organizer results are non-degraded. The corrected Gemini request contract works. Search expansion found three relevant videos in the initial pass, including the missing foundational sources. This is neither a no-match result nor query-order failure.
- Root cause: The initial incline source's Pro selector completed, while the two other already-found selectors ended with Google `ClientError` HTTP 499 at about 59 seconds. The first authoritative organizer therefore received only the two incline clips and could not invent unavailable foundations. The continuation later recovered `F=ma`, easy-problem, friction, and free-body-diagram candidates, but lesson metadata and organizer membership are generation-local: prior releases are supplied only as semantic coverage, not as reorderable reel IDs. AF-158 then correctly treats a plain continuation response as an append-only delta. No contract exists for a later healthy organizer to publish a new chain-wide order for the still-unseen prior tail while preserving the watched prefix.
- Universal fix: Keep the early partial release, but on a plain continuation pass the existing organizer the current candidates plus prior authoritative clips that are not durably seen. The prior IDs are mandatory but reorderable, so Gemini can place newly recovered prerequisites and concepts before those applications without dropping already-released inventory. The continuation still releases only its current-generation delta; a separately validated `reconciliation_tail_reel_ids` plan is persisted and returned through final events, status, replay, cached responses, and authoritative feed reconstruction. Unknown, duplicate, blank, partial, or out-of-inventory plans fail closed to AF-158 append order. Lesson prompt/cache advance to `lesson_order_v13`/11 and generation requests advance to `adaptive_clip_concepts_v6`, preventing pre-fix cached jobs from being reused.
- Active-scroll race rule: The browser recomputes its locked prefix when the final plan arrives using the greater of the active index and watched frontier. If a server-snapshot “unseen” reel became active while Gemini was planning, that reel never jumps or moves backward. IDs already inside the live locked prefix are ignored while applying the plan; the recovered prerequisite is placed immediately after that prefix and only the remaining unseen union is reordered. This intentionally preserves playback continuity over retroactively perfecting material the learner has already reached.
- Focused regression and latency proof: The combined organizer regression recovers foundations after an earlier application, keeps the prior unseen IDs exactly once, releases only the new delta, and reconstructs the same tail through status, sanitized replay, and the authoritative feed. Omitted mandatory IDs consume only the existing bounded organizer repair attempt, then fall back without data loss. Frontend controls cover valid, missing, partial, duplicate, unknown, and active-scroll race plans while retaining adaptive/quiz replacement behavior. No search, provider call, database query on the healthy initial path, wait, or sleep is added; a plain continuation reuses its existing organizer call and ranked source-chain read.

### AF-164 — The configured Pro selector retry can have no dispatch window

- Status: Fixed locally; focused retry, cancellation, permanent-error, deadline, and cost regressions pass, with exact-SHA deployment replay pending
- Severity: High — a transient selector failure is advertised as retryable, but the first physical request can consume the entire phase, leaving no opportunity for the configured retry before a partial batch is finalized
- Reproduction: The live Pro selector reserves 60 seconds of its 120-second source deadline for the final audit. `generate_json_v3` gives attempt one `min(90 seconds, all remaining selector time)`, so the initial request owns essentially the full 60 seconds. In the AF-163 run, two calls ended near 59 seconds; the 504 had less than the five-second minimum retry window, and typed HTTP 499 is outside the current transient-status set, so neither dispatched an immediate retry. A later continuation recovered two sources, while another 504 remained deferred.
- Root cause: A logical `max_retries=1` is configured without partitioning its absolute deadline into physical-attempt windows. The typed transient classifier also omits provider/client-cancel status 499 even when the application's cancellation callback is false. Source-level continuation recovery is bounded separately, but it does not make the intra-step retry truthful.
- Universal fix: Keep the source's absolute 120-second ceiling and `max_retries=1`, but give the selector and final audit that same outer deadline while retaining the original 60-second first-selector window. Selector-slot admission, CountTokens preflight, cost admission, and physical attempt one all share that first-window deadline; the HTTP timeout is clipped to whatever remains after admission/preflight. Only a transient provider failure can let the already-configured second attempt borrow the unused audit window. A response that arrives after the healthy first window is rejected exactly as before, so it cannot silently consume the audit allotment. A cost ticket admitted after its attempt window is abandoned and reconciled as not dispatched. Typed 499 is transient only when the application's cancellation callback is clear, while application cancellation still exits before any retry. Ordinary permanent 4xx behavior is unchanged.
- Focused regression: After a simulated 40 seconds of admission/preflight, attempt one is capped at the remaining 20 seconds; a 499 or 504 at 59 seconds dispatches exactly one retry against the full remaining source deadline after the existing one-second backoff. A partial cost-admission wait from second 40 through second 55 recomputes the provider timeout to 5 seconds instead of retaining the stale 20-second value. A late nominally successful first response is rejected, and a cost admission that crosses the first deadline makes no provider request and reconciles `dispatched=false`. SDK request-configuration failure after admission also reconciles that ticket as not dispatched and makes no provider request. Application cancellation after 499 makes one request and no sleep, permanent 400/401/403/404/422 responses make one request and no sleep, and the retry plus audit each reconcile a separate physical cost ticket while consuming one logical selector and one logical audit allowance. The focused Gemini client and Pro-selector gate passes 115 tests.

### AF-165 — A material-scoped organizer plan is rejected by a grouped feed

- Status: Fixed locally; grouped reconciliation and complete frontend verification pass, with exact-SHA deployment replay pending
- Severity: High for grouped study sets — a valid continuation plan is silently ignored whenever unseen reels from another material are present, preserving the earlier globally incorrect lesson order
- Reproduction: With live rows `[locked-a, old-a, old-b]`, material A returns `new-a` plus the valid plan `[new-a, old-a]`. The old validator compares those two planned A IDs with the three-row global tail `[old-a, old-b, new-a]`, rejects the length mismatch, and renders the append-only order `[locked-a, old-a, old-b, new-a]`.
- Root cause: The backend organizer and `reconciliation_tail_reel_ids` are intentionally scoped to one material/generation, while the browser validated exact plan coverage against every unseen row in the combined feed. The earlier grouped-feed test mocked reconciliation and therefore could not expose the contract mismatch.
- Universal fix: Both generation-settlement paths now pass the generating material ID. Exact validation considers only locked and unseen IDs owned by that material. On success, the planned rows replace only that material's existing unseen slots; foreign-material rows keep their exact indices and relative order. Missing, ambiguous, duplicate, blank, unknown, or partial plans still fail closed to append-safe behavior, and the latest active/watched prefix remains immutable.
- Focused regression: The real reconciliation callback transforms `[old-a, old-b, new-a]` with A's plan into `[new-a, old-b, old-a]`, retaining the same foreign B object in the same slot. The active-scroll race, invalid-plan matrix, transport forwarding, TypeScript contract, and other feed tests remain green.

### AF-166 — Fresh production physics falls back after both organizer models return an invalid order

- Status: Fixed locally with organizer salvage, cache, retry, telemetry, and active-scroll race regressions; exact-SHA deployment replay pending
- Severity: High — the candidate pool contains the requested foundations, derivations, and problems, but the learner receives deterministic fallback order instead of an AI-selected curriculum
- Reproduction: Post-reset material `37bd7e91-b603-4b78-8bdb-17dfb17cae50` requested intuition and free-body diagrams through `F=ma`, followed by progressively harder problems including an incline. Initial job `d4995ccb-fee8-4bc8-bbae-3515dc03b5be` released eight reels after 125.851 seconds. The Lite organizer and Flash organizer each returned HTTP 200 but were recorded as `invalid_model_order`; generation `b4bb2320-eb58-440e-9de7-15bb50ad900a` persisted `degraded=true`, `fallback_reason=invalid_model_order`, and a fallback sequence ending with an off-request rotational-law clip.
- Live quality observation: The fallback sequence begins with an appropriate inertia/`F=ma` explanation but then jumps into friction and angled-force problems before the simpler incline derivations; persisted clips span 58.77 to 502.29 seconds. The 502.29-second clip is one complete angled-force worked problem with a grounded beginning and result, so length alone is not a defect under the explicit any-length indivisible-problem contract.
- Confirmed quality scope: The rotational `tau=I alpha` clip is a relevance defect in the released feed, but not a selector false positive: it is related supporting inventory that the organizer may omit. The degraded fallback released it only because both organizer plans were rejected. The incline-with-friction context defect is recorded and fixed separately in AF-167.
- Live continuation evidence: Continuation job `1248edad-e8a4-403f-8463-7626c4bc5c87` completed with six new clips and persisted the same 13-ID `reconciliation_tail_reel_ids` in its generation and final event. The plan contained all six new IDs plus seven still-unseen prior IDs and omitted the one prior clip completed before ordering finished. The resulting plan starts with recovered intuition and a simple force/mass example, then incline components, derivations, and increasingly difficult problems. This proves the cross-batch organizer receives both prior unseen inventory and the latest durable seen state.
- Active-scroll race policy: A committed reel move writes `activeIndexRef` synchronously, so reconciliation freezes that reel and all earlier rows; no organizer insertion can move the visible clip. If reconciliation commits first, or a recall gate has not yet committed the move, the next scroll follows the improved order and lands on the inserted prerequisite. This is intentional: committed viewing wins, otherwise the organizer wins. Active-first, organizer-first, and pending-gate regressions all pass.
- Root cause: Both provider responses parsed successfully with HTTP 200/`STOP`, so this is a semantic order-validator rejection rather than model availability or schema parsing. The batch had eight unique known IDs, no required IDs, no declared chains or prerequisites, no temporal overlaps, and no prior-objective evidence. The organizer validates clip selection, checkpoints, prior-restatement declarations, terminal markers, same-source chronology, and dependencies atomically. Any locally repairable auxiliary or ordering violation discards the complete AI-selected subset and releases every input through fallback, which reintroduced the peripheral rotational clip. The current `invalid_model_order` telemetry collapses those predicates, and rejected raw responses are intentionally not persisted. A replay using production-derived learner/prompt metadata was blocked by the execution safety reviewer and was not retried, so the exact historical predicate cannot be recovered safely.
- Universal fix: Preserve Gemini's selected known subset and deterministically repair only mechanically provable constraints: dependency/chain closure, same-source/dependency topology, checkpoint membership/order, evidence-safe restatement membership, terminal-marker survival, and overlap filtering. Empty, duplicate, unknown, over-limit, or missing-required selections remain unsalvageable and use the existing bounded Gemini retry; a required clip omitted by the model is never inserted locally because only the organizer can choose its semantic position. Exhausted retries retain the existing required-aware availability fallback. Cache reads protect overlapping required IDs exactly as cache writes do, so a repaired continuation does not pay another organizer call. Successful repairs persist privacy-safe predicate names under `validation_repairs`; rejected plans persist `validation_failures`; neither contains prompt text, response text, nor reel IDs. No domain-specific rule, topic matcher, provider call, or healthy-path wait was added.
- Focused retest: The generic eight-ID/three-source reproduction preserves the AI's seven-clip subset, repairs chronology/checkpoints/restatements in one call, and keeps the peripheral eighth clip omitted. Required dependency closure, inverse foundation/application omission, exhausted required-aware fallback, overlapping-required cache write/read, terminal-summary projection, unsalvageable retry diagnostics, cross-source AI-order preservation, over-limit dependency-closure retry, and cached-plan validation pass. Lesson ordering plus generation integration passes 353 tests; the combined affected backend gate passes 1,102 tests; the three active-scroll race tests and complete 83-test feed suite pass.

### AF-167 — A selector can label a context-dependent continuation as standalone

- Status: Fixed locally with a grounded Gemini context-dependence audit and truthful transient retry; exact-SHA deployment replay pending
- Severity: High — a clip can be individually relevant yet begin with unresolved notation and references to an omitted prior explanation, so adaptive omission or reordering exposes an incomplete lesson step
- Reproduction: Reel `ingest-1b9ea8725e8b49d9` (`ufgY237M5KQ`, 314.880–429.120) opens with `now sometimes` and says one force is downward `as well`; later it uses `the normal force as we mentioned before`. The preceding source unit at 253.954–312.720 and its immediate neighbor establish the axes and the omitted force-component meaning. Nevertheless the selected reel persisted `self_contained=true`, `is_standalone=true`, no prerequisite IDs, and no chain.
- Root cause: The compact Gemini selector supplies the only standalone verdict. The high-reasoning Pro audit can reject unrelated, filler-dominated, or factually incorrect clips, but its schema and prompt cannot identify a context-dependent span. The selector therefore produced a semantic false positive that no later AI gate could correct; the audit call for this source also ended in a transient 504, although that did not create the missing verdict capability.
- Universal fix: Audit prompt/schema v11 adds the narrow `reject_context_dependent` verdict for indispensable context outside the returned span. The existing exact 5–10-word quote validator remains the authority: selector labels, scores, or local lexical/anaphora rules cannot reject a clip. A same-objective edge repair that supplies the setup must remain `KEEP`; when the indispensable setup lives only in a separately complete earlier unit, the audit omits only the dependent candidate. The selector prompt now also tells Gemini to set `stand=false` for that semantic case. Audit attempt one retains the original shared deadline and one-call healthy behavior; only a transient provider failure may use a bounded 60-second second-attempt grace, so a late 504 has a real retry without changing successful TTFR.
- Focused retest: A generic baseline/extension transcript proves grounded context-dependent omission while retaining the standalone prior unit; the existing boundary-repair control proves same-objective expansion remains `KEEP`. A simulated clock advances a first audit attempt from second 60 to second 119, returns HTTP 504, and proves exactly one physical retry succeeds in the grace window with separate cost reconciliation. The combined Pro selector/audit suites pass 749 tests, Gemini transport passes 105, and five healthy/retry latency guards pass in 0.97 seconds.

### AF-168 — Feedback refresh discards verified unseen inventory and regenerates exact duplicate clips

- Status: Fixed locally with monotonic source-inventory reuse and canonical exclusion regressions; exact-SHA deployment/adaptation replay pending
- Severity: Critical — after thumbs or quiz adaptation, revisiting or refilling the material can hide the already-paid unseen lesson and persist the same video/time clips under new reel IDs
- Reproduction: Physics job `cc8dfc04-54cc-4906-a73c-5a8745992b8d` released ten reels in generation `f382134d-2cf1-479f-bd1b-d54a021b577b`. Helpful feedback on the first reel changed the adaptation fingerprint and added its video to the exclusion cursor. The feedback refresh then returned only the watched reel. A refill created root job `6c8b010a-7051-4778-9eba-71d3c2f951f0` with no `source_generation_id`; generation `2ec64557-be1f-471c-a996-cbd685e9cb64` persisted six exact `(video_id, t_start, t_end)` duplicates of the prior generation's unseen clips under new IDs.
- Root cause: Exact completed-result reuse and verified source-inventory reuse share an overly strict compatibility rule. `_verified_cross_request_source_generation` rejects the immediately prior generation when either its adaptation fingerprint differs or its prior exclusion list is not exactly equal to the current list. Those checks are correct for returning a stale completed editorial result, but incorrect for supplying verified candidate evidence to the current organizer: feedback necessarily changes the fingerprint and monotonically adds the watched source to the cursor. The page also clears its in-memory continuation token during adaptive reranking, so no other source link survives a revisit. Frontend identity dedupe can hide duplicates only while both batches coexist in one mounted session; it cannot recover the inaccessible prior generation after replacement or reload.
- Universal fix: Keep `_latest_compatible_generation_job` exact so a stale adaptive result is never returned. For cross-request source inventory only, allow a different adaptation fingerprint and reuse only when the prior canonical exclusion set is a subset of the current set; `yt:<id>` and bare YouTube IDs compare identically. Exact learner, material, content, request-schema, language, Creative Commons, duration, concept/remediation, relevance, and verified-chain constraints remain. The current organizer and acquisition ranking still receive the new feedback/quiz state and larger cursor; reverse and incomparable cursors remain incompatible. No provider call, database query, retry, or wait is added.
- Focused retest and live replay: Empty-to-one and nonempty-to-larger cursors reuse verified source inventory across adaptation fingerprints; reverse, incomparable, and extra-current completed-result cases do not. Prefixed/bare video-ID forms compare canonically. The generation-job API suite passes 210 tests and the complete backend collection passes 2,936 tests plus 44 subtests. Replay thumbs-up, thumbs-down, quiz-correct, and quiz-wrong after the exact fix SHA is live.

- Severity: High — Gemini Pro can independently collapse several explicitly named concepts into one broad obligation, allowing the organizer to mistake an agenda/list mention for substantive coverage of every requested unit

The organizer released an overview plus detailed glycolysis and Krebs clips, but omitted that only detailed oxidative-phosphorylation clip. All four rows shared one obligation: `Explain Cellular Respiration steps: Glycolysis, Citric Acid Cycle, and Oxidative Phosphorylation`; the overview's phrase “three major steps; glycolysis” therefore made the same key appear covered even though it only listed the stages.

The validated constraints are discarded. No local topic splitter, provider call, search query, retry, or wait is added.

### AF-170 — An automatic continuation reconsiders and releases a cross-source strict restatement

- Status: Fixed locally with adaptation-scoped organizer restatement persistence and surfaceability guards; focused/full regressions pass, with exact-SHA replay pending
- Severity: High — a fill pass can override the immediately prior organizer's omission and place a shorter semantic duplicate into the same unseen lesson even though no learner signal changed
- Reproduction: Software generation `161e18b2-766b-4936-ae4c-f952f7c24d64` released a 74.615-second `finally` explanation covering unconditional execution plus resource-cleanup use cases, while its healthy one-call organizer omitted a different-source 7.600-second clip that only says `finally` always executes. Immediate child generation `8a536266-511e-4de1-bae1-db20477c80e6` acquired no new media, reconsidered the omitted reservoir row, selected it, and published a reconciliation tail placing the 7.6-second restatement directly after the richer `finally` clip. Both jobs used the same adaptation fingerprint.
- Root cause: A continuation reloads every verified source-chain candidate except authoritative delivered IDs; it does not retain the prior organizer's current-batch editorial omissions. Delivered-but-unseen reels correctly become mandatory reorderable IDs and are excluded from prior-history evidence, while the earlier omitted candidate returns as optional. Same-source overlap guards cannot and should not decide cross-source semantics. The richer and shorter clips also carry different concept-family and obligation identities because the shorter selector grouped `try, except, else, and finally`, so the generic Gemini restatement instruction was insufficient and the second organizer selected both.
- Universal fix: Lesson organizer v14 explicitly returns validated `current_restatement_reel_ids` only for optional candidates whose full educational contribution is contained in selected or required inventory, regardless of source/title/concept/family/obligation identity. The result, exact adaptation fingerprint, and selected guard IDs persist with the generation. A same-adaptation continuation suppresses only those AI-declared rows while their guard inventory remains current, delivered, or durably seen; changed adaptation reconsiders them. Release-limit, level, weak-quality, missing-context, and genuinely additive omissions are explicitly ineligible. No matcher, embedding, provider call, retry, query, or wait is added.
- Focused retest and live replay: A required rich explanation dominates a different-source/different-obligation strict subset while retaining a new application; same-adaptation continuation suppresses the subset and changed adaptation re-enables it. The 105-test lesson-ordering suite and complete backend collection pass. The organizer payload then truncates every transcript to its first 1,000 normalized characters and the compact prompt may truncate that head again. The middle and end are not sampled.
