### AF-172 — Terminal request punctuation fragments one Gemini-grounded obligation

- Status: Fixed locally with exact terminal-comma canonicalization; focused and complete backend regressions pass, with live law replay pending
- Severity: High — punctuation introduced while serializing one request phrase can split a single grounded curriculum facet into two obligation identities, making a broad clip look like the only witness for an otherwise-covered unit
- Reproduction: The law request produced two obligation rows at the same `source_start=55`: `causation (including proximate cause),` and `causation (including proximate cause)`. Their exact phrase hashes differed solely because one Gemini-derived phrase retained the list delimiter. The broad 166.51-second umbrella clip was the only candidate carrying one of those duplicate keys, so local mandatory reconciliation treated it as unique coverage.
- Root cause: `intent_obligation_key` hashes the cleaned source slice byte-for-byte, including one terminal ASCII comma that is syntactic request-list punctuation rather than semantic content. Source position already preserves occurrence identity; the delimiter therefore created a false second obligation without distinguishing a real concept. Internal punctuation, symbols, case, and distinct source offsets can remain meaning-bearing and must not be broadly normalized.
- Universal fix: Remove exactly one terminal ASCII comma after the existing whitespace cleanup before hashing the request phrase. Preserve source start, all internal punctuation, every other terminal character, case, and symbols. No domain words, fuzzy matcher, model call, query, wait, or extra latency are introduced.

All four focused identity controls and the complete backend collection pass. ### AF-173 — Corrective Gemini Pro audit exhausts after only two physical attempts

- Status: Fixed locally with an opt-in three-attempt transient audit budget; recovery, cost, permanent-failure, healthy-latency, and full-suite regressions pass
- Severity: High — two different transient provider failures can consume the entire corrective audit path even though the requested reliability contract is three to five attempts, leaving a recoverable broad boundary unaudited
- Reproduction: The law source's corrective Pro boundary audit sent attempt one, received HTTP 504, then sent one retry that raised `ReadTimeout`. With `max_retries=1`, the audit exhausted after two physical calls and correctly failed open to useful clips, including the broad umbrella candidate. A third bounded attempt was never available even though the provider failures were transient.
- Root cause: The shared retry transport supports explicit physical-attempt accounting, but `_audit_pro_boundaries` configures only one retry. That contradicts the requested three-to-five-attempt reliability policy for a step failure. Availability behavior is otherwise correct: selector output is retained when the corrective audit cannot complete.
- Universal fix: Configure only the corrective Pro audit for two retries, yielding at most three physical attempts, and opt it into the shared transport's full retry budget for any already-classified transient. Default callers keep the prior non-503 one-retry cap. The audit preserves its single-call healthy path, absolute deadline, per-attempt timeout/cost reconciliation, fail-open selector result, and no-retry behavior for permanent validation/configuration failures. This adds no healthy-path call, query, sleep, or streaming delay; only an already-failing audit may spend one additional bounded recovery attempt.
- Focused retest and live replay: A simulated `504 → ReadTimeout → valid structured audit` dispatches exactly three physical attempts with two retries and shrinking timeout windows; default transport controls retain their old cap. Seven explicit latency/retry guards, the 1,088-test selector matrix, and the complete backend collection pass. Replay the same law case and verify transient recovery without making an empty feed or delaying healthy TTFR.
- Superseded availability policy: AF-181 preserves this shared three-dispatch recovery ceiling but replaces fail-open selector release after audit exhaustion. Current-contract unresolved candidates remain retryable source inventory instead of being published as trusted clips.

### AF-174 — A persisted restatement omission can outlive the selected clip that justified it

- Severity: High — if a richer selected clip later fails the current surfaceability contract, blindly retaining its shorter subset's omission marker can remove both explanations from a same-adaptation continuation

- Root cause: `current_restatement_reel_ids` identifies omitted rows but does not persist which selected inventory must remain authoritative for that omission. Local reconciliation and later ranked-feed revalidation can remove selected clips independently, while `_same_adaptation_current_restatement_reel_ids` previously trusted the flat marker solely by adaptation fingerprint.

On continuation, suppress omitted IDs only while the full guard set is still surfaceable, authoritatively delivered, or durably seen. ### AF-175 — A full unseen reservoir never receives the new feedback or quiz signals

- Status: Fixed locally with immediate old-inventory response plus one current-adaptation child; four-signal worker and frontend race regressions pass
- Severity: Critical — thumbs and quiz outcomes can change the durable adaptation fingerprint while the learner continues seeing the prior organizer order, so the advertised adaptive behavior is delayed until the old reservoir is depleted
- Reproduction: The browser's adaptive rerank clears the continuation and reloads pages with `autofill=false`. AF-168 now correctly finds the prior verified generation, but the feed reads `released_only=true`, restores that generation's authoritative release order, and returns a full nine-reel reservoir. Because no shortfall exists and autofill is disabled, no current-request child is queued; versioned rows bypass the legacy local adaptive ordering. The response therefore contains the new fingerprint's request context but the old fingerprint's editorial plan.
- Root cause: AF-168 separated source-inventory compatibility from exact completed-result compatibility, but job submission still treats generation solely as a missing-inventory operation. It has no full-reservoir path for applying a changed adaptation fingerprint to already-verified candidates. The organizer receives feedback/quiz signals only inside a worker job, so a page read cannot produce a current-signal order by itself.
- Universal fix: Adaptive reloads now opt into the existing background autofill path. Cross-request lookup exports the matched prior request metadata from its existing row read; when page one reuses a source whose adaptation fingerprint differs, feed submission creates one linked child even if the nine-reel reservoir is full. The HTTP response still returns old unseen inventory immediately with that job ID. A full reservoir sets no fresh-source budget, so the worker skips acquisition and runs only the existing current-signal organizer; partial inventory retains the existing bounded top-up. Same-fingerprint mode/relevance reuse does not create organizer work. No provider call or additional database query runs in the HTTP path.
- Focused retest and live replay: Parameterized helpful, confusing, quiz-correct, and quiz-wrong full-reservoir cases each return nine old reels immediately, queue exactly one current-fingerprint child, call no organizer in the HTTP request, perform no worker acquisition, and pass their exact current signals to one organizer call. ### AF-176 — Nested retry layers can exceed the documented three-attempt audit ceiling

- Status: Fixed locally with one shared three-dispatch audit budget; composition, healthy, transport, cost, and full affected suites pass
- Severity: High — one corrective audit can reserve more cost and time than intended during provider instability, contradicting the three-to-five-attempt requirement and the streaming-latency guard
- Reproduction: AF-173 gives each `_call_model` audit invocation two transport retries, or three physical dispatches. `_audit_pro_boundaries` separately permits two structured-schema attempts, and an invalid semantic audit contract recursively invokes the same two-attempt function once more. Without a shared counter, the composed worst case is twelve physical Gemini dispatches before deadline exhaustion.
- Root cause: Transport, structured-schema, and semantic-contract retries each enforce a local bound but do not share one step-level physical-attempt budget. Existing focused tests mock `_call_model`, assert only its local `max_retries`, and therefore cannot observe the multiplication.
- Universal fix: Share one three-dispatch counter across transport, structured-schema, and recursive contract recovery. Before every `_call_model`, derive its retry allowance from the remaining physical budget; after success or schema failure, debit actual `physical_dispatches`. Schema or contract recovery runs only while budget remains. One healthy dispatch, existing retryability/permanent-failure rules, fail-open selector output, deadlines, and attempt-scoped cost reconciliation remain unchanged.
- Focused retest and live replay: A three-dispatch transport/schema composition cannot enter its second schema layer; a two-dispatch invalid contract leaves exactly one call for recursive recovery. The focused regression set passes 7 tests, Pro-audit/Gemini retry subset passes 84, and complete affected files pass 855. `504 → ReadTimeout → valid` still recovers in three; healthy behavior remains one call.
- Superseded availability policy: AF-181 changes only the terminal disposition after this shared budget is exhausted: the current contract fails closed for release and keeps the source retryable. The three-physical-dispatch composition ceiling remains authoritative.

### AF-177 — Expansion caches an AI intent contract before validating downstream grounding

- Status: Fixed locally with the exact selector trust gate on live and cached expansion contracts; adversarial and full affected suites pass
- Severity: High — a malformed positioned phrase or relationship graph is labeled authoritative upstream context, then silently disappears at clipping time, recreating the independent compressed-summary reparse that AF-169 is meant to remove
- Reproduction: Expansion validates unique IDs, references, summary/query coverage, and ordered topic-term presence, but not exact source occurrence, duplicate positioned identity, joint relation kind, or relationship span topology. Such a response can be written to v12 cache. The Pro path's stricter `_trusted_request_intent_from_settings` then returns `None`; every video falls back to contractless Pro parsing of the compressed summary.
- Root cause: The new transport contract and the pre-existing selector authority use different validation gates. The former decides cacheability before the latter proves that the exact original request mechanically grounds the AI layout. Missing `source_occurrence` is also defaulted for compatibility after the live provider schema required it, so raw shape validation alone is insufficient.
- Universal fix: Before returning or caching a Gemini expansion, validate the completed v1 dictionary through the exact existing downstream selector authority. Preserve unset-field provenance on the live model so an ambiguous missing occurrence cannot default into trust. Failure consumes the already-bounded second expansion attempt; exhaustion uses the literal original-request fallback, never the compressed summary with a discarded contract. Cache reads use the same authority and treat malformed rows as misses. This is exact structural validation, not semantic matching, and adds no provider call, query, wait, or heuristic.
- Focused retest and live replay: Wrong/missing repeated-phrase occurrences, duplicate positioned identities, invalid relation kinds/topology, and malformed cached contracts fail before transport; valid repeated phrases, joint comparisons, named lists, and cross-domain notation round-trip. Practice retrieval passes 110 tests, expansion/practice/segment-cache passes 149, full production selector passes 749, and downstream handoff passes 3. Healthy expansion remains one provider call with no retry sleep.

- Severity: High — feedback and quiz mastery for one displayed reel can be attributed only to Newton's second law even though the reel substantially teaches first-law inertia as well, while the organizer can omit the standalone first-law reel as redundant

The same row nevertheless carries grounded obligations for the overall three-laws subject, first-law inertia/equilibrium, and second-law math. The successful `pro_candidate_audit_v11` call approved this source on its first physical attempt. Feedback and quiz persistence correctly remain scalar; making mastery multi-valued would instead contaminate every supporting/task/scope concept.
- Universal fix: Add an explicit objective-fulfillment lane to the existing selector/audit response while retaining current evidence as relevance/support. Only fulfilled objective IDs become mandatory organizer obligations. Mechanically reject one scalar objective claiming multiple sibling subject/scope objectives unless a trusted upstream joint structure names those members and its relation is also fulfilled. If mandatory reconciliation restores an atomic clip, pass the existing original topic into its fallback ordering so explicit `A then B` edges place A first. This preserves genuine comparisons/syntheses, one-concept adaptive attribution, and contextual clips with no extra healthy-path call, query, wait, or sleep.
- Focused retest and live replay: Fulfillment-only obligations, support-only connections, scalar sibling rejection, genuine joint-synthesis controls, and role/directness/coverage transport pass across physics, biology, math, software, and law. ### AF-179 — One empty literal search exhausts a common topic with retry capacity unused

- Status: Fixed locally with bounded AI zero-search recovery; exact biology production replay pending

The generation pass limit is one with zero allowed no-growth passes, and `max_attempts=3` applies only to raised provider errors, so the empty result becomes terminal while four logical searches and two durable attempts remain.
- Universal fix: Keep the healthy one-pass path and AI ownership. ### AF-180 — `Generate Reels` cannot restart a terminal empty generation

- Status: Fixed locally with one validated manual terminal-empty retry identity; exact browser replay pending
- Severity: High — the only recovery action offered by the empty-feed UI appears interactive but leaves the learner permanently on the same terminal result
- Reproduction: After AF-179 reached `inventory_exhausted`, the production feed displayed a unique enabled `Generate Reels` button. Clicking it left the same `No reels yet` state. A post-click database read showed exactly one job for material `85b94ffb-127b-481a-90f7-173ed85cc6f0`: the original exhausted job `b6cdb606-3d15-4328-97f7-16e4ba660e0a`; no queued or running retry was created.
- Root cause: The UI always renders the button enabled, but terminal bookkeeping sets the material in `generationFinishedRef` and `canRequestMore=false`; `bootstrapFirstReels(true)` then exits before making a request. Even if that frontend gate is bypassed, the exhausted job ID remains the continuation token. Backend completed-job lookup intentionally includes compatible `exhausted` rows, and both continuation and exact-request paths return the same no-source-work terminal job rather than enqueueing. Clearing only the client gate or token therefore cannot recover.
- Universal fix: Preserve ordinary reload/autofill reuse to prevent loops, but add a narrowly validated manual terminal-empty retry identity carrying the exhausted job ID. The client permits this one locked action, clears only that material's terminal marker, and omits the continuation token. Backend verifies the referenced job belongs to the same learner/material/concept/settings and is exhausted with no released reels; it reuses any already-active ordinary request-key job or bypasses only that one empty terminal row and creates a fresh root job. The existing active-request uniqueness collapses double clicks. Healthy/nonempty generation remains unchanged.
- Focused retest and live replay: Root and continuation terminal-empty retries, active-job reuse, changed-setting rejection, stale-terminal rejection, and authoritative-nonempty rejection pass in the complete 221-test generation-job API suite. The frontend action remains scoped to one locked request. Exact browser replay after deployment must still prove one click queues one job and recovered clips stream.

### AF-186 — A second adaptive rerank loses the ancestral reservoir and reacquires duplicate sources

- Status: Fixed locally with recursive unseen-release reconciliation; focused and complete generation-job regressions pass, exact production replay pending
- Severity: Critical — consecutive feedback turns can hide still-valid unseen ancestor clips from the organizer, so a partial adaptive child searches without giving Gemini the reusable teaching inventory that should constrain its selection and progression
- Reproduction: Helpful feedback first created organizer-only generation `090845b0-6335-42f0-8043-e9eea3b2de81` with `source_generation_id=221d15c3...`, zero newly persisted reels, and an editorial plan referencing its ancestor. Confusing feedback then created child `8abbc4db-4a42-4399-af09-37b4e18d012d`. Read-only production reconstruction proved the recursive inventory count and ranked loader already crossed that zero-row node. The root held twelve authoritative clips: four from video `nR1kMuT03Wg`, seven from `kKKM8Y-u7ds`, and three from `y61M8kpWu88`. Job `a0d641a6-3aed-4544-a8a6-4385d9bce3d7` explicitly excluded the first two source videos, so only three of nine requested clips remained reusable and a bounded six-clip top-up was legitimate. The defect was that those three valid unseen `y61M8kpWu88` clips were also removed before Gemini, leaving the organizer unable to consider them alongside the top-up.
- Root cause: `_filter_continuation_release_temporal_overlaps` composed every authoritative ancestor release into the same set used as consumed/delivered history. A release is not a learner view: ancestor clips can be released yet still unseen. Treating all released IDs as consumed stripped ranked, current-contract, non-excluded unseen rows before organizer selection. The earlier one-hop-count explanation was disproven by the production data and recursive code trace.
- Universal fix: Preserve explicit source-video exclusions and durable seen/completed progress, but load authoritative source releases recursively through every zero-row organizer node and split currently valid unseen rows into mandatory organizer candidates in their latest editorial order. Optional current/new rows remain separate. Allow an empty physical child to persist `ordered_reel_ids=[]` plus a validated reconciliation tail, and compose that tail through later descendants. A full unexcluded ancestry stays organizer-only; a partial ancestry such as three of nine performs exactly one bounded six-clip top-up and sends all three reusable clips plus the new rows to Gemini.
- Focused retest and live replay: Helpful→confusing and quiz→feedback chains through zero-row children retain unseen releases; two empty nodes preserve the newest editorial tail; durable seen and explicitly excluded source videos remain unavailable; a three-of-nine chain performs one six-clip top-up; and a full eligible ancestry skips acquisition. `backend/tests/test_generation_job_api.py` passes 217 tests. Replay both an unexcluded full-reservoir chain and the exact two-video-exclusion case after deployment.

### AF-187 — One adaptive signal scans every historical reel's family JSON

- Status: Fixed locally with one-row exact-concept profiles; persistence, promotion, conflict, adaptive, same-concept scale, and worker regressions pass, deployed latency replay pending
- Severity: High — after the first thumb or quiz outcome, ranking and organizer preparation can parse every reel row for the material, making adaptive latency grow with unrelated historical inventory
- Reproduction: `_learner_adaptation_context(..., propagate_concept_families=True)` calls `_persisted_concept_family_profiles`, which executes `SELECT concept_id, search_context_json FROM reels WHERE material_id = ?` and decodes every returned JSON object. The fresh-learner guard avoids this only before any signal exists. A ranked-feed request can call the same propagation path once during scoring and again during curriculum ordering.
- Root cause: Trusted family equivalence is needed only between exact feedback/quiz source concepts and concepts present in the current organizer or ranked candidate set, but the profile reader has no scoped, canonical persistence surface. Restricting the old reel query to relevant concept IDs still leaves it linear in every historical reel for one popular concept, and boundary-state promotion can replace a reel's family JSON without reconciling the derived identity.
- Universal fix: Persist one authoritative profile row keyed by the unchanged exact scalar `concept_id`. A validated current Gemini family write is idempotent only when material, contract, authority, and canonical identity agree; any mismatch marks the profile permanently conflicted without overwriting its original identity, and readers fail closed on conflicted rows. Reel insert and successful boundary-promotion CAS reconcile the profile in the same transaction; failed CAS and retained candidates do not change it. Runtime reads query only signal-source plus current organizer/ranked candidate IDs from the indexed profile table, making work O(relevant concepts) with zero historical reel JSON parsing. Fresh-reset legacy reels receive no unsafe backfill. Exact attribution and the exact-ID adaptation fingerprint remain unchanged.
- Focused retest and live replay: Four hundred valid 512-byte reel JSON rows for the same relevant concept persist exactly one profile and the post-feedback reader returns at most one row per relevant concept while retaining helpful same-family ordering; a fresh learner performs no profile query. Repeated family writes and same-family promotion stay unconflicted; family, material, contract, authority, and promoted-family mismatches preserve the original identity and fail closed; failed boundary CAS leaves the profile byte-for-byte unchanged. The acquisition-concept/clip-specific-concept promotion path updates only the effective clip concept. Adaptive curriculum plus persistence integrity pass 60 tests and 7 subtests. Deployed post-feedback latency comparison remains pending.

### AF-188 — Worker sanitization strips the new organizer semantics

- Severity: Critical — selector and organizer unit tests can pass while production silently drops Gemini's objective-fulfillment, supporting-connection, relationship-witness, curriculum-edge, role, directness, and coverage metadata before the organizer receives a clip

Both `_public_generation_reel(..., preserve_lesson_order_metadata=True)` and `_finalize_request_reel_order` therefore remove those trusted fields on the worker path.
- Root cause: The private metadata allowlist was not advanced with the selector/organizer contract. The schemas changed together, but the sanitization seam between them remained on the prior field set.
- Universal fix: Advance the exact allowlist with only the organizer-consumed current-contract fields and add a worker-level regression proving the full trusted payload survives into the organizer while unrelated private fields remain stripped.
- Focused retest and live replay: All three checkpoint-preparation worker variants preserve the six new trusted fields plus the existing obligation field into `order_lesson_batch`, strip an unrelated private field, and strip every private selection field from the public final event. Production replay remains pending.

### AF-189 — Nonempty YouTube search can still terminate with zero valid clips

- Status: Fixed locally with one failure-only AI source-recovery pass; exact cross-domain production replay pending
- Severity: Critical — one to three discovered videos can all fail transcript, selector, audit, or boundary admission, after which the job returns an empty feed even though search and novel YouTube inventory remain

- Root cause: Discovery success is incorrectly treated as clip success. The recovery trigger exists above source analysis, so it cannot observe the actual user-visible zero-clip outcome; no failure-only analysis ticket is reserved for a novel AI-expanded source.
- Universal fix: After and only after the initial source set yields zero valid clips, run one explicit Gemini recovery expansion with the exact request, tried queries, and rejected source IDs. Search only novel AI queries and analyze at most one additional fast source or two additional slow sources, for total ceilings of three and five. Reuse the same provider/deadline/cost budgets, never add a healthy-path call, and stop after the single recovery pass.

### AF-190 — Manual retry rejects an exhausted continuation batch

- Status: Fixed locally with immutable-dimension/current-batch validation; all manual-retry regressions pass, production replay pending
- Severity: High — the empty-feed retry button works for an exhausted root job but returns HTTP 409 for an exhausted continuation, leaving a later empty batch unrecoverable
- Reproduction: The frontend intentionally omits `continuation_token` when it submits `retry_terminal_job_id`. Backend validation compares the referenced terminal job's continuation-bearing `request_key` with the new tokenless root key, which can never match. Existing tests exercise only an exhausted root.
- Root cause: Manual retry identity is coupled to the request key even though removing the exhausted continuation token is the safety mechanism that creates a fresh recovery root.
- Universal fix: Validate learner, material, concept, content, current-batch position, and every immutable request dimension from the terminal job parameters instead of continuation-token key equality. Reject an older replaced terminal, reuse a compatible active recovery, and submit the valid retry as a tokenless fresh request.
- Focused retest and live replay: The four manual-retry API regressions pass. An empty exhausted continuation now creates a tokenless fresh root, an immediate repeated click reuses that active recovery, changed settings and a simultaneous continuation token are rejected, a newer compatible terminal invalidates the stale retry, and an exhausted job with an authoritative release remains ineligible. Production replay remains pending.

### AF-191 — Mandatory organizer reconciliation can lose an explicit `A then B` request

- Severity: High — Gemini can select payoff B while mandatory reconciliation restores prerequisite A after it, leaving B→A even when the learner explicitly requested A then B

The prior same-source test passes only because chronology independently produces A→B.
- Root cause: The request-level sequence contract is not threaded across the final mandatory/model-repair seam, so reconciliation validates coverage but forgets the explicit learner ordering instruction.
- Universal fix: Pass the unchanged topic only into mandatory reconciliation. When reconciliation inserts/restores a clip and both that clip and a retained model selection map to the explicit request sequence, let the existing constraint-safe fallback order those mapped concepts. Do not apply request-text ordering to a healthy complete Gemini plan or salvage path; valid cross-source model order remains authoritative without a trusted curriculum edge. No model call is added.

### AF-192 — An idle empty feed creates a fresh root immediately after bounded terminal failure

- Status: Fixed locally with frontend/backend authorization regressions; exact production replay pending
- Severity: Critical — a background feed can bypass the three-attempt terminal ceiling and spend a second full request budget without explicit learner intent
- Reproduction: Fresh circuits material `12743c77-5de9-42d2-9c70-29b132e80da8` created job `a79e5f1f-d70c-4f16-99cf-c2d687965cb1`. Transient Gemini 503/504 failures exercised the same durable job through attempts one, two, and three; attempt three reached successful fresh-source selections but exhausted the configured provider budget during final audit and terminated at `2026-07-22T17:43:14.076693Z` with `provider_budget_exceeded`, no reels, and one terminal event. The signed-in browser remained idle. At `2026-07-22T17:43:14.332892Z`, only 256 ms later, a new root job `e6a37c62-f2b5-4a86-8fd2-de480b9541be` was created and started without a click.
- Expected: Passive SSE settlement, polling, refresh, or empty-state rendering must expose the terminal result and wait for the explicit `Generate Reels` action carrying `retry_terminal_job_id`; only that action may create one validated fresh root.
- Root cause: The SSE `failed` terminal deleted the active frontend job and released the generation lock but did not synchronously close the startup-bootstrap latch. With zero reels, the startup effect immediately called `bootstrapFirstReels(false)` and submitted an ordinary tokenless `POST /api/reels/generate`. The backend compounded the race by treating any current compatible failed global-provider terminal as implicit authorization for a fresh root. Production proves the second job was that direct POST rather than a continuation or feed autofill: both jobs share the same request key and have no source lineage, while the second stores `continuation_token: null` and lacks the feed-only `fresh_source_budget` field. Existing request-key coalescing covers only queued/running jobs, and explicit terminal retry previously accepted only `exhausted`, so the failed job could neither block the passive POST nor be retried through the explicit contract.
- Universal fix: Close the existing passive-bootstrap latch synchronously for `failed` and `cancelled`, retain the failed terminal job ID separately from active-job state, and send it only from an explicit empty-state retry. At the API boundary, require `retry_terminal_job_id` before replacing a current compatible empty global-provider failure, while extending the same validated terminal-retry path from empty `exhausted` to that failed class. Preserve active retry coalescing, immutable request matching, stale/replaced-terminal rejection, and released-output rejection. No provider call, sleep, or successful-path branch is added.
- Focused retest and live replay: The exact failed-SSE-before-consumer-release race now closes the passive latch and retains the durable retry identity; terminal reload and direct-generation status paths do the same. A passive tokenless POST returns `409 terminal_retry_required` without creating a job/event, attaching quota, charging the submission rate limit, checking billing, or waking the worker. One explicit retry creates a tokenless replacement, a repeated explicit action coalesces to it, and stale, settings-mismatched, released, or continuation-combined retries fail closed. The focused frontend/API set passes 118 tests; the complete frontend passes 198 tests, typecheck and production build pass; the generation API/job suites pass 268 tests. The complete backend/pipeline gate passes 3,698 tests, 1 skip, and 48 subtests, the secondary backend gate passes 739 tests, and six healthy-path one-call/no-sleep guards pass. Exact production circuits replay remains pending.

### AF-193 — The first terminal-ID frontend fix overgeneralizes failed retries and misses nonempty continuations

- Status: Fixed locally with one server-authoritative explicit handshake across empty/nonempty and root/continuation feeds; production replay pending
- Severity: High — an explicit learner retry can be permanently rejected after a non-global failure, or after a global-provider failure that occurs while earlier reels remain visible
- Reproduction: The first AF-192 frontend patch retained and submitted `retry_terminal_job_id` for every `failed` status, but the backend intentionally authorizes that contract only for empty failed jobs whose error code is in `JOB_GLOBAL_PROVIDER_ERROR_CODES`. A `provider_transient`, `generation_failed`, or other non-global terminal therefore reaches the manual Generate action, sends an ineligible terminal ID, and receives `409 invalid_terminal_retry` even though an ordinary explicit request may legally resume its source work. Separately, the error-banner Retry action uses the terminal path only when `reels.length === 0`; after a global failure on a later batch, it calls ordinary `requestReadyBatch`, which receives `terminal_retry_required` forever. A later failed continuation also leaves the prior successful continuation token cached: resending that token enters the backend continuation branch and skips the tokenless latest-failed guard, so a passive tail request can create another continuation without explicit authorization.
- Root cause: The frontend inferred backend retry eligibility from the coarse `failed` status and tied explicit-terminal retry to empty-state rendering. Retry eligibility actually depends on server-owned terminal error/release state, while explicit learner intent is independent of whether prior reels are still present. The backend guard was also applied only to tokenless submissions rather than to the exact request identity of a repeated continuation.
- Required universal fix and focused retest: Keep the failed/cancelled passive-bootstrap latch, but do not duplicate the backend error enum or assume every failure is terminal-ID retryable. Route both empty and nonempty explicit actions through one server-authoritative bounded handshake: the first probe preserves any cached continuation so non-global failures retain the ordinary legal child-recovery path; a global-provider terminal can return its current ID without writes, and the same explicit learner action may then submit exactly one tokenless validated retry with that ID. Passive bootstrap/refill must never perform this handshake. Apply the same terminal gate to an exact repeated continuation request before any new job/quota/wake. Add separate empty/nonempty, root/continuation, global/non-global, stale/released, repeat-click, and successful-partial controls before rerunning the complete gates.

### AF-194 — Replaying a stale continuation can discard the failed child’s source-attempt lineage

- Status: Fixed locally with exact failed-child lineage and bounded source-attempt preservation; production replay pending
- Severity: High — older/passive clients can bypass failed-source retry accounting and reanalyze the same source beyond its intended bound
- Reproduction: Root A completes, continuation B (whose request key includes token A) fails after recording retryable or exhausted source attempts in generation B. Repeating token A validates A and currently seeds the next job from A’s generation. Although the exact-key lookup now sees B, it uses B only for global-provider authorization and does not carry B’s result generation into the non-global recovery. The new job therefore omits B’s source-attempt chain.
- Root cause: The continuation branch fixes `source_generation_id` from the supplied parent token before consulting the latest exact request-key terminal, while the tokenless failed-job path correctly resumes the latest failed generation and enforces its accumulated failed-source ceiling.
- Required universal fix and focused retest: For an exact failed continuation with reusable source work, override lineage with that failed child’s result generation; when its failed-source attempts are exhausted, return the same bounded `source_retry_exhausted` result as the tokenless path. Preserve first continuation, completed/partial cache reuse, global explicit retry, and generic failures with no reusable work. Add separate retryable and exhausted A→B→repeat-A regressions proving B lineage and attempt counts cannot be skipped.

### AF-195 — A passive later-batch terminal can remain invisible behind populated or provisional inventory

- Status: Fixed locally with authoritative terminal visibility and explicit-retry regressions; production replay pending
- Severity: Critical — after a passive tail job fails, the learner can keep swiping into repeated non-authorizing `409 terminal_retry_required` responses without ever receiving the manual Retry action that is allowed to perform the server-authoritative handshake
- Reproduction: Begin with at least one playable reel, trigger passive `requestReadyBatch(..., surfaceError=false)`, and let its current generation consumer terminate `failed` or `cancelled`. When no candidate was emitted, the zero-result branch suppresses `noteFeedFailure` because the feed is nonempty and the request is passive. When at least one candidate was provisionally emitted before the same terminal, `generated.length > 0` bypasses the failure branch entirely. In both cases the terminal status is recorded, but no visible error/Retry control appears; the next passive tail request remains non-authorizing and repeats the backend conflict.
- Root cause: Error visibility is inferred from final candidate count, `surfaceError`, and whether the whole feed is empty instead of from the authoritative terminal status of the current later-batch consumer. Provisional candidate delivery therefore masks its job's terminal failure, while the nonempty zero-result path treats that failure like an ordinary background miss.
- Universal fix: Track the authoritative `failed`/`cancelled` callback within each active consumer, independently of candidate count. Surface that consumer's terminal error on populated feeds before either the zero-result or provisional-result settlement path; feed-owned durable consumers use the same rule. Passive requests retain their non-authorizing continuation behavior. Only the rendered manual Retry marks its first probe explicit, while both passive and first explicit probes preserve cached continuation lineage. Only a subsequent server-directed terminal-ID retry clears continuation.
- Focused retest and live replay: Runtime callback tests cover a populated passive tail failing with zero candidates, failing after one provisional candidate, and cancelling after one provisional candidate. Each preserves the old continuation passively with `explicitUserRetry:false`, exposes the real terminal error, then performs one displayed manual retry with `explicitUserRetry:true`, the same continuation, and no client-inferred retry ID. The feed-owned failed consumer also exposes its terminal before releasing the lock. AF-196/AF-197/AF-202 extend this same runtime matrix through restored and cross-tab terminal evidence; the focused frontend/API collection passes 134, the complete frontend passes 214, and TypeScript validation passes. Exact production replay remains pending.

### AF-196 — Clearing continuation on the first explicit probe discards failed-child source budgets

- Status: Fixed locally with lineage-preserving first-probe and directed-retry regressions; production replay pending
- Severity: Critical — a generic, retryable non-global, or cancelled continuation child can lose continuation worker semantics; even when the backend retains B's source generation, `is_continuation=false` can inherit a spent completed-ancestor budget and silently produce no replacement clips
- Reproduction: Root A yields continuation token A; continuation child B consumes source attempts and then fails or is cancelled. The AF-193/AF-195 frontend revision removes token A from the learner's first explicit probe. The backend's tokenless latest-compatible path can retain B's `source_generation_id`, but the worker no longer treats the request as a continuation. With A's source budget already spent, remaining source budget can become zero and the recovery can terminate without provider work or output. A global-provider child does require a tokenless terminal-ID replacement, but only after the backend identifies that exact child and returns `terminal_retry_required`.
- Root cause: Client-side continuation removal conflates two distinct recovery contracts: the ordinary explicit continuation probe that preserves B lineage and continuation budget semantics, and the server-directed global terminal replacement that intentionally starts a validated tokenless root.
- Universal fix: Preserve cached continuation on passive requests and on the first explicit failed/cancelled probe. Let the backend exact-child guard return `terminal_retry_required` only for a global-provider terminal; then and only then may the API's single directed retry clear continuation and add `retry_terminal_job_id`. Generic, retryable non-global, and cancelled explicit recovery remain one continuation POST.
- Focused retest and live replay: Page runtime tests prove passive and first explicit failed/cancelled probes carry the same child continuation. API tests prove a global handshake's first body carries that continuation while its one directed terminal-ID body clears it; successful and unrelated explicit continuation requests remain one POST and retain the token. The backend A→B→repeat-A regression selects B lineage, persists `continuation_token=A`, coalesces C, and directly leases C to prove the spent ancestor does not suppress its fresh continuation retrieval budget. Generic failed/no-work and cancelled child controls create/reuse one C, while global children retain their no-write terminal gate. The focused backend recovery/global controls pass 10 and the complete generation API/jobs suites pass 276; the focused frontend collection passes 134, the complete frontend passes 214, and TypeScript validation passes. Exact production replay remains pending.

### AF-197 — Restored terminal state can fail before a new stream callback and remain hidden

- Status: Fixed locally with restored failed/cancelled pre-callback visibility regressions; production replay pending
- Severity: High — a populated feed restored with `failed` or `cancelled` terminal state can repeatedly receive a passive backend conflict without exposing the manual Retry action
- Reproduction: Reload a populated feed whose authoritative `lastTerminalStatus` is already `failed` or `cancelled`, then run a passive tail request. If `generateReelsStream` rejects during submission, such as with `terminal_retry_required`, no new `onTerminal` callback fires. The per-call `terminalFailed` flag stays false, so AF-195 treats the error as an ordinary suppressed background failure even though the material's restored terminal state is authoritative.
- Root cause: AF-195 recognizes only terminal evidence emitted during the current consumer and ignores the already-restored per-material terminal status used by the retry contract.
- Universal fix: Treat a failed request row as terminal-actionable when either its current consumer observed `failed`/`cancelled` or its material already has that recorded terminal status. Ordinary transport failures without terminal evidence remain suppressed on populated passive feeds.
- Focused retest and live replay: Populated runtime controls restore both `failed` and `cancelled`, reject before any new terminal callback, expose the actual failure, and prove passive plus displayed first explicit probes retain continuation with only the latter setting `explicitUserRetry:true`. A separate nonterminal background failure remains hidden. These controls are included in the 134 focused and 214 complete frontend passes; TypeScript validation passes. Exact production replay remains pending.

### AF-198 — Tokenless terminal-ID source recovery can inherit a spent ancestor budget

- Status: Fixed locally with persisted budget semantics and direct worker dispatch regression; production replay pending
- Severity: Critical — an explicitly authorized retry can link the exact retryable failed source yet perform no source analysis, leaving the learner with an empty replacement batch
- Reproduction: Root A completes after consuming its source budget; continuation B terminates `exhausted` with one retryable `failed_source_attempts` entry. The learner submits the intentionally tokenless `retry_terminal_job_id=B` contract. The backend correctly selects B's result generation as the replacement source, but persists neither a continuation token nor `fresh_source_budget`. The worker therefore sees `is_continuation=false`, inherits A/B's analyzed-source total, computes zero remaining budget, and never dispatches the bounded source retry.
- Root cause: The submission layer preserves source lineage for validated terminal-ID recovery but does not persist the continuation-equivalent budget entitlement required by the worker's existing `is_continuation or fresh_source_budget` gate.
- Universal fix and focused retest: Only a validated terminal-ID retry that actually reuses a retryable source generation now persists `fresh_source_budget=true`. The completed-A/exhausted-B regression proves tokenless C links B, retains its accumulated failed-source attempt, coalesces on repeat, and directly dispatches one worker retrieval with the slow-mode bounded source budget. Tokenless global-terminal replacement remains source-free. The 10 focused recovery/global controls pass, and the complete generation API/jobs suites pass 276 tests.

### AF-199 — Feed-owned retryable source recovery can inherit a spent ancestor budget

- Status: Fixed locally with retry-source-only feed marker and direct worker dispatch regression; production replay pending
- Severity: Critical — passive feed refill can repeatedly create a linked recovery batch that performs no provider work even though the failed child has a legal bounded source retry
- Reproduction: Root A completes after consuming its source budget; continuation B fails or exhausts with retryable source work. `/api/feed` selects B as `retry_source_job` and links C to B's result generation, but C carries neither a continuation token nor `fresh_source_budget`. The worker treats C as an ordinary root, inherits the completed ancestor's analyzed-source budget, computes zero remaining budget, and skips retrieval.
- Root cause: Feed recovery records source lineage but omits the worker-facing budget semantic that distinguishes one authorized linked retry from ordinary cross-request cache reuse.
- Universal fix and focused retest: Feed autofill now persists `fresh_source_budget=true` only when it creates a job from a verified retryable failed/exhausted source (or the existing qualified cross-request top-up rule). The completed-A/failed-B regression proves feed C links B, coalesces without a fourth job, and directly dispatches the bounded worker retrieval despite A's spent budget. Healthy cache reuse and passive global-provider suppression remain unchanged. The 10 focused recovery/global controls pass, and the complete generation API/jobs suites pass 276 tests.

### AF-200 — Ordinary tokenless retryable-source recovery can inherit a spent budget or replay an older completion

- Status: Fixed locally with linked-retry budget marker and newest-active precedence; production replay pending
- Severity: Critical — an ordinary direct recovery can either perform no source analysis or return completed root A while the authorized recovery C is already queued
- Reproduction: A compatible terminal job has retryable failed/exhausted source state and its generation chain has already consumed the normal source budget. A tokenless `POST /api/reels/generate` correctly creates C linked to that terminal generation, but C lacks both continuation and `fresh_source_budget`, so its worker computes zero remaining budget. If older root A is completed under the same tokenless request key, an immediate repeated POST finds active C and completed A; the latest-compatible branch selects C as active without clearing A, and the later completed-cache return replays A instead of coalescing C.
- Root cause: Direct retryable-source lineage selection is not coupled to the worker-facing fresh bounded-budget entitlement, and queued/running latest-compatible precedence does not invalidate an older exact-key completed candidate.
- Universal fix and focused retest: A newly created direct job linked specifically from verified retryable failed/exhausted state now persists `fresh_source_budget=true`. A newest compatible queued/running row clears only the older completed candidate before cache return. The completed-A/failed-B regression proves tokenless C persistence, immediate repeat coalescing to C instead of replaying A, retained B attempt lineage, and direct worker retrieval with the bounded source budget. Completed-only cache reuse, normal cross-request rules, continuation semantics, and global-terminal no-write behavior pass the full 276-test generation API/jobs gate.

### AF-202 — A cross-tab terminal conflict is hidden when local status is stale

- Status: Fixed locally with exact-code classification and cross-tab runtime regressions; production replay pending
- Severity: Critical — another tab or consumer can terminalize continuation child B while this populated feed still records `partial` or no terminal status, causing passive stale-A conflicts to repeat without exposing the only Retry action allowed to perform the server-directed handshake
- Reproduction: Keep a populated feed locally at continuation A with `lastTerminalStatus=partial` or absent. Let another consumer create and terminalize exact child B with a global-provider failure. The local passive stale-A probe receives `409 terminal_retry_required` before `generateReelsStream` can emit `onTerminal`. AF-197 sees neither a same-call terminal nor locally recorded `failed`/`cancelled`, so it suppresses the error. Even if displayed by another path, the manual probe currently sets `explicitUserRetry` only when local status is failed/cancelled, preventing the API handshake under the same stale-state condition.
- Root cause: Frontend visibility and explicit learner intent are inferred exclusively from tab-local terminal state, while the backend's exact-child conflict is the authoritative cross-consumer signal.
- Universal fix: Treat only the reviewed 409 generation-terminal contract codes `terminal_retry_required`, `source_retry_exhausted`, and `invalid_terminal_retry` as actionable independently of local status; arbitrary conflicts remain suppressed. Pass first-probe `explicitUserRetry` from the displayed learner action itself rather than from local status, while preserving continuation. The API still handshakes only on exact `terminal_retry_required`.
- Focused retest and live replay: A runtime cross-tab control starts locally at `partial`, receives pre-callback `terminal_retry_required`, exposes it, then sends displayed Retry with `explicitUserRetry:true` and the same continuation. API body assertions prove the first POST preserves the token and the single directed retry clears it. Exact-code controls accept the three reviewed terminal outcomes but reject arbitrary 409 and wrong-status lookalikes; unrelated explicit errors remain one token-preserving POST. The focused collection passes 134, the complete frontend passes 214, and TypeScript validation passes. Exact production replay remains pending.

### AF-203 — Gemini 3 query expansion sends an unsupported raw Pydantic schema

- Status: Fixed locally and verified against the production model/key; exact-SHA deployed reel replay pending
- Severity: Critical — the first fresh cross-domain production run exhausted all three durable attempts with zero clips, so relevance, progression, and adaptation cannot be accepted even though the retry controller behaved correctly
- Reproduction: Fresh DC-circuits material `39047452-94cd-4456-88dd-13207b7c3691` created root job `95eb2425-2659-4838-aa04-8a8788d7429d` at `2026-07-22T19:22:02.022844Z`. Every recorded Gemini expansion dispatch ended `dispatch_failed:ClientError`; one Supadata search succeeded but the later searches returned HTTP 400 `provider_request_rejected`. Two cached transcripts reached Gemini Pro segmentation, but transport timeouts, 504s, a contract rejection, and a final non-retryable 400 left no admitted clip. The job exhausted attempt 3/3 at `19:28:28.873440Z` with `inventory_exhausted` and zero reels. The explicit `Generate Reels` action then created exactly one replacement job, `71255168-101d-4fcf-bbbf-5785a28f0f03`, at `19:31:05.688184Z`; it immediately reproduced the expansion `ClientError` and search 400 while reusing the two cached transcripts.
- Expected: Gemini compression/expansion must yield usable universal search queries, and a stable request/schema incompatibility must be identified rather than silently falling back to the long literal learner request on every attempt.
- Root cause: `_practice_fast_gemini_raw_async` passes `_PracticeFastExpansion.model_json_schema()` directly as `response_json_schema`. That raw Pydantic schema contains `minLength`, `maxLength`, and other validation keywords outside Gemini GenerateContent's documented structured-output subset. The selector paths already pass their Pydantic schemas through `backend.gemini_client._gemini3_json_schema`, which strips unsupported provider keywords while retaining application-side Pydantic validation; expansion bypasses that sanitizer. A production-key model metadata request returned HTTP 200 for `gemini-3.1-flash-lite`, a minimal structured/thinking request returned 200, the exact raw expansion schema reproduced HTTP 400 `INVALID_ARGUMENT`, and the identical exact prompt/model with the existing sanitizer reached the model with HTTP 200. This rules out subscription tier or model unavailability.
- Universal fix and focused retest: Expansion now uses the existing Gemini 3 schema sanitizer while retaining strict local Pydantic/selector validation, and dispatch telemetry records the real provider status. The wire-schema regression proves unsupported keywords are absent while every semantic field remains required. The affected expansion/search/cumulative-diagnostics collection passes 189 tests, and the production-key schema request now reaches Gemini instead of returning HTTP 400.

### AF-204 — A semantic/provider failure is falsely reported as “No matching YouTube videos were discovered”

- Status: Fixed locally for both normal exhaustion and typed-provider terminalization; exact-SHA deployed reel replay pending
- Severity: High — the learner is told that YouTube has no matching inventory and may broaden a valid request even though retrieval found videos and transcripts; the false terminal reason also obscures the provider/semantic defect that actually needs recovery
- Reproduction: Exhausted circuits job `95eb2425-2659-4838-aa04-8a8788d7429d` persisted `inventory_exhausted` with the user-facing message “No matching YouTube videos were discovered.” Its terminal payload reports zero discovered videos, but the same job's authoritative cumulative usage records four discovered videos and four usable transcripts. Those transcripts reached Gemini Pro segmentation/audit, where transport and semantic-contract failures rejected every candidate.
- Expected: A zero-inventory terminal is valid only when discovery truly found no videos. When videos/transcripts exist but no clip survives segmentation, audit, or boundary admission, the terminal state must preserve that distinct failure stage and actionable provider/semantic reason without claiming YouTube inventory is absent.
- Root cause: `generation_usage_payload()` correctly merges `previous_counters` into cumulative durable usage, but final release separately sets `stage_counters = context.counters()` from only the current/final attempt. It passes those last-attempt counters to both `_generation_exhaustion_message(...)` and `terminal_error_json`, so attempt 3's zero discovery overwrites the four videos and transcripts recorded by attempts 1–2.
- Universal fix and focused retest: Final exhaustion now classifies and persists the counters already merged by `generation_usage_payload()` rather than final-attempt-only counters. The exact three-attempt regression records four discovered videos and four usable transcripts in attempts one/two, zero discovery plus a Gemini empty result in attempt three, and proves the terminal selects content-quality guidance with all cumulative counts intact. No successful-path branch or provider call changed.

### AF-205 — An in-flight adaptive rerank can move the reel the learner just swiped into

- Status: Fixed locally for the active/watched race and full-capacity released-inventory preservation; exact-SHA deployed adaptation replay pending
- Severity: Critical — thumbs/quiz adaptation can violate the watched/active-prefix lock, remove or reorder a clip at the moment it becomes watched, and snap the viewer back to a previously active reel
- Reproduction: `rerankUnseenTail` captures `currentIndex`, `preservedThroughIndex`, `currentActiveReelId`, and `watchedPrefix` before awaiting the adaptive `/api/feed` request. Feed navigation remains enabled while that request is in flight. If the learner swipes from the captured active clip into a previously unseen clip before the response returns, the success path applies `updateSessionReels(nextReels)` built from the stale prefix and resolves the active index from the stale active ID. The later generated-tail reconciliation recomputes a live frontier, but this immediate rerank response does not.
- Expected: Once a clip becomes active or watched, no in-flight organizer/rerank response may insert before it, remove it, or move it. Adaptation may affect only the live unseen suffix, and the viewer must remain on the live active reel.
- Root cause: The request correctly snapshots exclusion inputs for the server, but the client incorrectly reuses the same snapshot as the mutation frontier after an asynchronous response. Feedback buttons are guarded by `pendingAction`; swipe navigation is intentionally not, so the mutation frontier must be recomputed at response time.
- Universal fix and focused retest: The response now recomputes the active reel, watched frontier, source exclusions, and mandatory prior unseen suffix from live refs immediately before mutation. The deferred A→C swipe regression proves the active/watched prefix cannot move or disappear while the organizer request is in flight. Feed tests pass 98/98, the full frontend passes 216/216, typecheck and production build pass, and the change adds no request, await, timer, sleep, or stream-start work.

### AF-206 — Expansion semantic retries repeat the same prompt and fall back inconsistently across domains

- Status: Fixed locally with corrective AI retry and strict semantic mismatch rejection; exact-SHA deployed reel replay pending
- Severity: Critical — after the wire schema is accepted, a repairable Gemini field inconsistency can still discard the entire compressed intent/query plan and send the long literal request to YouTube, reproducing narrow/stale inventory on valid non-physics topics
- Reproduction: With AF-203's sanitized wire schema, biology and Python-exception prompts returned valid AI query plans. A derivative prompt succeeded on a later run but fell back after both responses on the first run. The negligence-law prompt returned HTTP 200 twice yet fell back both times because Gemini labeled the `soft difficulty progression` constraint as `kind=format` while also setting its redundant `relationship_topology=ordered`; the strict downstream contract requires `not_applicable` for every non-relationship kind.
- Expected: A schema-valid but semantically inconsistent response receives a bounded corrective Gemini retry that names the violated contract. It must not repeat the identical prompt and hope for random success, and a healthy first response must remain one call with no wait.
- Root cause: `expand_query_practice_fast` retries statusless local validation failures, but every attempt calls `_practice_fast_gemini_raw` with the identical system/user prompt. The model never sees the validation failure it must correct. The expansion ceiling is also two attempts even though this task's requested bounded corrective ceiling is three to five.
- Universal fix and focused retest: Expansion now has one shared three-attempt ceiling and sends a compact payload-free validation reason only after a local semantic/schema rejection. Safe normalization removes a redundant relationship ID only when at least two real members remain; every kind/topology mismatch remains a strict contract error for Gemini to correct. Healthy output is still one call with no wait, permanent 4xx responses remain one call, and production-key circuits/biology/math/software/law plans all return Gemini queries and trusted intent contracts.

### AF-207 — Exhausted Gemini expansion silently switches to a literal heuristic

- Status: Fixed locally with typed failure propagation and a tested GA Flash fallback; exact-SHA durable retry replay pending
- Severity: Critical — when Gemini cannot produce a selector-valid compressed intent after its bounded attempts, retrieval silently searches the learner's uncompressed literal text and labels it trusted, defeating the required Gemini compression/expansion contract and making retry behavior look successful while discarding semantic structure
- Reproduction: The exact production-key cross-domain matrix intermittently exhausted local semantic validation for math, software, or law. `expand_query_practice_fast` then returned `provider_used=literal_fallback` with the original text instead of exposing the failed Gemini step. `discover_practice_fast` subsequently searched that literal value, so the durable three-attempt generation controller could not classify or retry expansion as a provider-response failure.
- Expected: A healthy response remains one Lite call. Recoverable failures receive at most three calls with compact corrective context, including a final call to a fixed supported non-Pro Flash model. If no Gemini response satisfies the universal intent contract, the step must raise a typed retryable provider-response failure; permanent provider failures must retain their non-retryable classification. No domain keywords or deterministic semantic substitute may enter the production path.
- Root cause: Expansion catches every non-cancellation exception, stores only display strings, and unconditionally returns `literal_fallback` after the loop. It neither retains the final typed exception nor routes the last bounded attempt to the already configured full Flash model, so the surrounding durable job cannot distinguish semantic failure from a valid expansion.
- Universal fix and focused retest: Attempts one/two use `gemini-3.1-flash-lite`; attempt three uses the explicit GA `gemini-3.6-flash`, never an environment-selected Pro model. Lite 404 moves directly to the alternate model. Exhausted local contracts and zero-result recovery raise `ProviderResponseValidationError`; transport/408/5xx, 429, auth, quota, 404, and permanent 4xx map to their typed classes using payload-free detail. Focused status, recovery, no-literal, Pro-isolation, and healthy-one-call controls pass. The former `gemini-3.5-flash` fallback repeatedly returned Google's explicit high-demand 503; the production key completed the same circuits contract with 3.6 Flash, and all five domains then passed.

### AF-208 — A rejected Supadata cursor falsely claims another search branch ran

- Status: Fixed locally with truthful branch-neutral diagnostics; exact-SHA production replay pending
- Severity: High — terminal diagnostics say retrieval continued with another grounded query even when no alternate query existed, obscuring the actual inventory/recovery state during an empty feed
- Reproduction: The circuits run loaded a cached first page with an opaque continuation token. Supadata rejected that token with HTTP 400, and `_continue_provider_pages` emitted “continued with another grounded search query.” In the failing expansion state, both the remaining page frontier and novel recovery queue were empty, so no later search request was dispatched.
- Expected: Cursor diagnostics must state only what occurred. Skipping an invalid cursor may be reported immediately; claiming a continuation or alternative search requires evidence that such a request actually ran.
- Root cause: The exception branch constructs success-oriented warning text before inspecting or dispatching any later frontier entry.
- Universal fix and focused retest: Cursor rejection now says only that the unusable branch was skipped. Separate sole-cursor and multi-branch regressions prove it never claims an undispatched query while still traversing a real alternate branch. The change adds no call, wait, or healthy-path work.

### AF-209 — A known-invalid opaque Supadata cursor is replayed across retries

- Status: Fixed locally with exact-key negative caching; exact-SHA production replay pending
- Severity: High — every recovery or durable job attempt can spend another search reservation and network round trip on the same provider-issued token already proven invalid, delaying fresh-source recovery and reducing the remaining search budget
- Reproduction: Both circuits jobs repeatedly reloaded the positive six-hour first-page cache entry and resubmitted the same continuation token, receiving the identical HTTP 400 “Invalid or expired continuation token” response. The in-memory traversal `seen` set prevented repetition only inside one call.
- Expected: Once Supadata explicitly rejects a page/continuation token as invalid or expired, that exact query/filter/language/token cache key should resolve as a short-lived terminal empty page. Other queries and fresh Gemini recovery branches remain eligible; unrelated 400s, authentication, quota, and transient failures must not be cached.
- Root cause: Successful first pages and their opaque token are cached, but cursor rejection state is neither persisted nor written to the existing negative-cache surface.
- Universal fix and focused retest: Transport and orchestration now share one narrow invalid/expired-token predicate. The first explicit matching 400 writes an empty terminal page under the exact token key and still raises; the second identical request is a cache hit with no HTTP dispatch or search reservation. A separate unrelated-400 control proves no negative entry is written. The existing 15-minute empty-result TTL bounds recovery, and healthy/valid cursors are unchanged.

### AF-210 — Corrective expansion feedback hides the missing sides of a relationship

- Status: Fixed locally and verified on circuits plus the production-key five-domain matrix; exact-SHA reel replay pending
- Severity: Critical — Lite repeatedly emits a relationship constraint as its own graph member plus only the governing subject, so the plan never declares the two actual sides/stages and exhausts corrective attempts before search
- Reproduction: Two independent circuits responses produced `member_constraint_ids=[compare, DC-circuits]` with `relation_constraint_id=compare` (and analogous progression output). The safe normalizer removed the redundant relation ID, after which Pydantic emitted only the generic “list should have at least 2 items” message. Attempt two received that message and reproduced the same invalid shape; the final Flash call then encountered a transient 503.
- Expected: `member_constraint_ids` contains at least two separately declared non-relationship side/stage constraints and never contains `relation_constraint_id`. A corrective retry must be told this exact universal contract so Gemini can add the omitted comparison members; semantic sides must not be fabricated locally.
- Root cause: The cross-field normalizer turns a precise self-membership/missing-sides violation into a generic post-normalization list-length failure, and the provider schema gives the two joint-structure fields no descriptions. The corrective prompt therefore lacks the distinction between relationship identity and relationship members.
- Universal fix and focused retest: Both provider fields now explicitly distinguish relationship identity from at least two separately declared sides/stages. If removing a redundant relation ID would leave fewer than two members, validation emits that exact compact correction; when two real members remain, safe normalization still succeeds. Strict selector validation and the shared three-call ceiling remain. The exact circuits wrapper returned twelve constraints, two valid joint structures, and three Gemini search queries; biology, derivatives, Python exceptions, and negligence law also returned trusted plans.

### AF-211 — Normalizing non-relationship topology can erase explicit teaching order

- Status: Fixed locally with strict rejection and production-key five-domain verification; exact-SHA deployed reel replay pending
- Severity: Critical — an ordered or directed learner requirement can be silently trusted as an unrelated format/scope constraint, so the organizer and selector lose the progression edge that should govern reel flow
- Reproduction: Validate `Teach alpha, then beta.` with a Gemini-style constraint labeled `kind=format`, `relationship_topology=ordered`, and no joint structure. `_ignore_topology_for_non_relationships` rewrites topology to `not_applicable`; the downstream trusted-intent gate accepts the contract even though no relationship constraint preserves the requested order.
- Expected: Conflicting semantic fields are a Gemini contract error and receive bounded corrective AI retry. Local code must not choose which meaning-bearing field is authoritative or erase the relationship.
- Root cause: The AF-206 normalization treated topology as redundant metadata whenever `kind` was non-relationship, but topology carries independent semantic evidence that the model may instead have mislabeled `kind`.
- Universal fix and focused retest: The semantic rewrite was removed, so every kind/topology mismatch is rejected and sent back through the same bounded corrective AI loop. An ordered-request regression proves the inconsistent first plan is never trusted and the corrected response retains the requested order. The real production-key matrix then succeeded for circuits, cellular respiration, derivatives, Python exceptions, and negligence law without a domain allowlist or added healthy-path work.

### AF-212 — Full-capacity reranking can truncate previously released unseen reels

- Status: Fixed locally with full/near-capacity and deferred-swipe regressions; exact-SHA deployed adaptation replay pending
- Severity: Critical — a learner can lose a reel that was already released but not yet watched when an adaptive organizer response adds enough new rows to hit the 50-reel session cap
- Reproduction: AF-205 builds `prefix + server tail + missing live unseen` and slices only afterward. With a near-full/full live session, genuinely new server rows occupy capacity before missing prior unseen rows, so the suffix is truncated despite being mandatory released inventory. The six-row swipe race cannot expose the cap.
- Expected: Every live watched/active row and every previously released unseen row survives reconciliation. The organizer may reorder or insert before still-unseen rows, but only genuinely new rows compete for the capacity left after all released inventory is reserved. If a formerly unseen row becomes active while awaiting the response, it is part of the live locked prefix.
- Root cause: Dedupe preserves identity but the capacity slice assigns priority by concatenation order instead of reserving slots for live released inventory.
- Universal fix and focused retest: Reconciliation recomputes unique live inventory after the await, reserves every watched/active and previously released unseen identity, and admits only the number of genuinely new server rows that fit the remaining capacity. Matching released rows still follow organizer order, while omitted released rows are appended intact. Full-capacity, near-capacity, and deferred A→C swipe regressions pass in the 98-test feed collection; TypeScript passes, and the change adds no request, wait, retry, timer, or stream-start work.

After retryable attempt three reaches its ceiling, `transition_generation_terminal` persists that cumulative usage but separately writes `error_detail.counters=context.counters()`, which contains only attempt three.

### AF-214 — Expansion warning logs can contain the rejected learner/model payload

- Status: Fixed locally with payload-redaction log regression; exact-SHA production log replay pending
- Severity: High — a semantic corrective failure can place the learner's exact request or Gemini-generated query text into production warning logs even though durable provider details were made payload-free
- Reproduction: `_PracticeFastExpansion.model_validate_json` raises a Pydantic error whose string includes `input_value`. `expand_query_practice_fast` appends full `str(exc)` for every attempt and emits the joined list at warning level on exhaustion.
- Expected: Operational logs contain only model, attempt, exception type, provider status, and a compact payload-free validation reason. Raw response values and learner text must never be logged from this path.
- Root cause: The retry prompt/detail sanitizer is applied after the full exception string has already been stored for logging.
- Universal fix and focused retest: Each warning summary is built only from model, attempt, exception type, provider status, and compact structural feedback; the full exception string is never stored or logged. ### AF-215 — The stronger corrective model can truncate a valid maximum-detail plan

- Status: Fixed locally and verified with the production-key five-domain matrix; exact-SHA deployed reel replay pending
- Severity: Critical — the final alternate model can satisfy the semantic correction yet return incomplete JSON, causing a retryable empty feed even though the request and model are otherwise valid

The shared 2,048-token cap was designed for Lite's concise normal output, while the schema permits up to sixteen detailed constraints plus joint structures and queries.

- Root cause: Primary and alternate models share one output cap despite different verbosity and the alternate being invoked specifically for a complex corrective response.

### AF-216 — Provider-side Gemini HTTP 499 bypasses the bounded expansion retry

- Status: Fixed locally with provider/application cancellation regressions; exact-SHA deployed retry replay pending
- Severity: Critical — a transient Google serving cancellation can terminate expansion immediately and empty an otherwise valid feed even though the application is still active and two bounded attempts remain
- Reproduction: `_practice_fast_failure_is_retryable` treats only 408, 429, and 5xx statuses as transient, and the permanent-error regression explicitly includes 499. The repository's established AF-164 Gemini policy distinguishes Google/provider HTTP 499 from application cancellation: provider 499 is retryable only after the caller confirms its own cancellation signal is clear. Expansion already performs that cancellation check before classification but still returns false for 499.
- Expected: A raw provider-side 499 with a clear application cancellation probe uses the same shared three-attempt expansion ceiling and maps to `ProviderTransientError` if exhausted. `CancellationError` and typed `GeminiCancelledError` remain immediate cancellation with no retry.
- Root cause: AF-207's expansion-specific status classifier copied the 408/429/5xx set but omitted the existing opt-in provider-cancel rule, while a stale test incorrectly codified 499 as a permanent 4xx.
- Universal fix and focused retest: Expansion treats raw provider HTTP 499 as transient only after `raise_if_cancelled` confirms the application cancellation probe is clear, and exhausted 499 maps to `ProviderTransientError`. Both application cancellation after a provider response and typed `GeminiCancelledError` convert immediately to `CancellationError` with one call and no retry. Provider-499 recovery, three-attempt exhaustion, typed mapping, and both no-retry cancellation controls pass in the 168-test expansion/retrieval collection; the healthy path is unchanged.

### AF-217 — Invalid-cursor warnings can log the learner's search text
