- Expected: The warning records only that a provider continuation cursor was rejected and its branch skipped; learner/model text remains absent from logs while the returned diagnostic stays truthful.
- Root cause: AF-208 corrected the user-facing sentence but retained pre-existing query interpolation in the operational warning.
- Universal fix and focused retest: The cursor warning no longer interpolates the query. A caplog regression drives an invalid sole cursor with a secret learner query and proves the operational event and truthful returned warning remain present while the secret is absent.

### AF-218 — Fresh broad-topic production generation exhausts selection before dispatch

- Status: Fixed locally with universal selector/audit and completion-budget regressions; exact-SHA production replay pending
- Severity: Critical — a signed-in Pro learner receives zero reels for a broad, explicitly structured DC-circuits request even though expansion, YouTube search, transcripts, and Gemini segmentation all returned successful provider responses
- Reproduction: After the scoped production reset, submit “Teach DC circuits from first principles: explain voltage, current, and resistance; derive and apply Ohm's law V = IR with correct units; compare series and parallel circuits; then solve a numerical circuit problem step by step. Build a clear progression from concepts to application.” Material `32d4b33b-bdd4-4fb8-9c2a-08db8c863359`, job `5911ca37-d472-4041-874f-252a4a79bff2`, found six videos and six usable transcripts, but failed after 283.05 seconds at durable attempt two of three and returned “Clip selection budget was exhausted before dispatch” with zero reels.
- Expected: The pipeline returns relevant clips whenever grounded YouTube inventory survives semantic validation. A recoverable stage may retry within the shared bounded ceiling, but the learner must not receive a misleading selection-budget terminal when no selector dispatch occurred; difficulty is soft and cannot prevent otherwise useful clips from being returned.
- Root cause: Attempt one spent its three-source Pro audit budget on high-thinking calls that took 104.8–163.4 seconds and ended in truncation, HTTP 504, or locally invalid audit contracts. The retry correctly preserved the same job and source ledger. On attempt two, Pro returned six relevant atomic circuit candidates, but every candidate overclaimed multiple sibling scope objectives and the deterministic fulfillment contract correctly rejected them as `objective_fulfillment_untrusted_sibling_umbrella`. The existing “corrective” selector then repeated the identical prompt without the rejection codes. Its dispatch was denied because prior known and billing-unknown Gemini exposure left about $0.12 under the fail-closed $2.50 ceiling; the non-retryable cost terminal therefore stopped the job at attempt two. YouTube scarcity, transcript scarcity, level filtering, duplicate filtering, and organizer omission are ruled out.
- Universal fix and focused retest: Objective/family/topology judgments that are structurally valid but semantically ambiguous now continue to the mandatory transcript-grounded Pro audit instead of being dropped by local semantic matching; malformed IDs and structural contracts still fail closed. Corrective selector/audit calls receive only bounded, payload-free rejection codes, and healthy first selector/audit calls use medium thinking while only logical correction raises thinking effort. A completion-only `$2` fast/`$3` slow ceiling can finish a same-source selector repair or mandatory audit after a logical selector exists, but cannot start expansion, a new source, or an orphan audit; logical and physical call ceilings remain unchanged. Successful selector telemetry is preserved when the later audit fails. The two changed selector/runtime collections pass 773 tests, the wider runtime/job/diagnostic regressions pass 497, and healthy selector/audit still uses exactly two calls with no retry. No domain keyword, circuits-specific exception, lexical matching heuristic, added healthy-path provider call, or unbounded retry was introduced.

### AF-219 — Completion retry ceiling is added across durable-attempt summaries

- Status: Fixed locally with a three-attempt merge regression; exact-SHA production replay pending
- Severity: High — enforcement remains bounded, but retry diagnostics can report a false `$6`/`$9` completion ceiling for a slow job whose actual hard ceiling is `$3`, corrupting budget-exhaustion analysis and learner-visible operational evidence
- Reproduction: Persist a provider failure and re-lease the same generation job for two further durable attempts. `generation_usage_payload` merges numeric summary fields from the prior usage into the current attempt; because `completion_cost_limit_usd` was not classified as a ceiling, each retry adds another copy of the same limit.
- Expected: Token/call/cost consumption is cumulative, while configured normal and completion ceilings remain the current authoritative budget values on every attempt.
- Root cause: AF-218 introduced the completion-only cost ceiling in provider usage, but the durable usage merger's explicit non-additive field set still contained only the pre-existing ceilings and exposure snapshots.
- Universal fix and focused retest: `completion_cost_limit_usd` is now non-additive alongside `cost_limit_usd`. The existing three-attempt transient-provider worker regression asserts after attempts one, two, and three that the summary ceiling exactly equals the authoritative current budget ceiling.

### AF-220 — Valid related inventory must survive audio and difficulty quality gates

- Status: Fixed locally with boundary-completion-order, finite-cap, organizer-payload, and fallback-only regressions; exact-SHA production replay pending
- Severity: Critical — a learner may receive zero reels even though at least one playable, transcript-grounded, related, coherent clip exists but has imperfect audio quality or a neighboring difficulty
- Reproduction: Give one source a structurally playable Gemini `best_effort` cut and a stronger `verified` or `context_aligned` cut, reverse their acoustic completion order, and constrain persistence to one row. The coarse cut could consume the slot first. The same failure remained across sources because deferral ended at the source boundary: a fast coarse source could consume `max_persisted_reels=1` and emit its callback before a slower stronger source completed. A non-surfaceable stronger row could also consume that finite storage slot before a valid fallback, and retry persistence classified the incoming evidence instead of the stronger row actually retained in the database. The first batch-wide repair still had a retry-order hole: with fresh fallback A before candidate B whose database row retained verified evidence, A could saturate either the finite storage cap or the ordinary `max_reels` output cap before B was inspected. A retained best-effort row could similarly fill the output list before a later retained stronger row, and returning on the first retained stronger row silently lost additional retained verified/context-aligned clips. In the release path, `_selection_boundary_status` was then stripped before the lesson organizer, so even an uncapped organizer could not distinguish a coarse fallback from a transcript-grounded or acoustically verified cut. Controls prove an off-level-only valid clip and a best-effort-only structurally playable Gemini clip both remain nonempty.
- Expected: `verified` and transcript-proven `context_aligned` clips are the normal lane. A structurally playable, related Gemini `best_effort` cut is retained only as the last-resort lane and must still produce a nonempty result when that lane is all that exists. Previously released unseen rows remain immutable. Relevance, finite playable range, transcript grounding, coherent context, and safety remain hard requirements; difficulty remains soft.
- Root cause: Boundary verification and persistence were interleaved, and the first fallback implementation scoped deferral to one source rather than the whole already-started batch. The first completed coarse fallback therefore still counted against cross-source persistence/release capacity and could emit before stronger pending work. Persistence capacity was also charged before surface eligibility was known, retry classification used the incoming instead of retained boundary state, and the direct ReelService adapter dropped that retained state. The initial batch-wide lane stopped scanning as soon as its fallback output filled and returned after its first retained stronger row, conflating output capacity with zero-cost inspection/reuse of existing rows. Release shaping then erased the boundary-evidence field before Gemini ordering, applied fallback removal before guarded editorial exclusions, loaded protected source releases only when one optional output collector was present, and treated only a new stronger row—not an already released stronger row—as sufficient to suppress a fresh fallback.
- Universal fix: Stronger candidates still persist and stream immediately. `best_effort` candidates now wait in one bounded batch-wide fallback lane and no longer satisfy the stronger-inventory acquisition threshold, so every already-running source gets its normal budget before fallback acceptance. Before that degraded lane stores or emits a fallback, it read-only preflights exact material/concept/source/generation/candidate identities, scans every retained candidate ahead of fresh fallback work, and collects all retained stronger rows up to the ordinary inventory cap; any such row suppresses the complete fallback set. This applies with finite persistence caps and production's uncapped persistence setting. Non-surfaceable rows cannot consume a finite output persistence cap; retry classification uses the boundary status returned from the retained database row; and direct ReelService output carries the same status. Healthy time-to-first-ready receives no new wait, call, search, sleep, or parent-release traversal; retained-row preflight runs only after the pipeline is already in the coarse degraded lane, while only mixed/fallback or editorial-risk release paths read source releases. Release filtering applies guarded editorial exclusions before choosing the fallback lane, preserves every authoritative released ID even without the optional collector, and removes fresh best-effort inventory whenever any stronger surviving row exists. The organizer now receives `boundary_evidence` (`verified`, `context_aligned`, or `best_effort`) and is explicitly required to use best-effort only as a nonempty last resort. The lesson prompt/cache contract advances to `lesson_order_v16`, and ranked-feed cache version `49` prevents reuse of rows that predate boundary evidence.
- Focused retest: Both completion orders × both stronger evidence kinds pass under a one-row same-source persistence cap; a true two-source finite-cap regression proves a fast best-effort source neither stores nor emits before a slower stronger source; a non-surfaceable row cannot starve the fallback; retained verified evidence wins retry classification with `max_persisted_reels=1` and `None`, in both fresh/retained orders; retained-best-effort before retained-verified still selects verified; two retained stronger clips (verified plus context-aligned) both survive when capacity permits; direct service output preserves and ranks the status; editorial exclusion cannot turn the surviving fallback into zero; released fallback rows remain immutable during reconstruction; a protected stronger row suppresses a fresh fallback; best-effort-only and adjacent-level-only pools remain nonempty; full/compact organizer payloads preserve all three evidence values; and the fallback-only lane now has a bounded first-ready path without dispatching extra sources once its valid inventory fills the request. The aggregate eight-file affected matrix passes 826 tests and 32 subtests.

### AF-221 — Cross-generation difficulty merge ignores the effective adaptive target

- Status: Fixed locally with root/child crossover regression; exact-SHA production replay pending
- Severity: High — quiz/thumb adjustment can move the effective target into a neighboring band while a continuation merge still orders the originally selected named band first
- Reproduction: Keep the selected level `beginner`, apply `global_adjustment=+0.20` so the effective target becomes `0.35` (intermediate), place one beginner clip in the root generation and one intermediate clip in its child, and force the deterministic cross-generation merge. The old merge returned beginner first.
- Expected: Acquisition, Gemini ordering, deterministic fallback, continuation merging, and final feed agree on the same effective target. With a neutral adjustment beginner remains first; after the crossover intermediate is first. Both clips remain valid inventory.
- Root cause: Per-generation adaptive ordering used the continuous effective target, but `_ranked_request_reels` converted only `selected_level` to a stage when merging already-ordered generation heads. The deterministic fallback API also accepted only the named level.
- Universal fix and focused retest: Derive the merge stage from `effective_level_target(selected_level, global_adjustment)` and allow deterministic inventory ordering to receive that same continuous target. The parameterized neutral/crossover root-child regression now passes without an additional provider call or hard level filter.

### AF-222 — Deterministic same-concept level repair can override valid pedagogy

- Status: Fixed locally by removing the unsafe repair; adversarial organizer-flow regression passes; exact-SHA production replay pending
- Severity: High — a post-Gemini numeric sort could turn a correct concept-orientation → worked-example lesson into example → orientation
- Reproduction: Give both a harder prerequisite explanation and an easier worked application the same persisted `concept_id`, ask for concept then application, and have Gemini return that valid order for a beginner target. The deterministic repair moved the easier application first even though the clips were not interchangeable and no trusted machine dependency existed to restore the pedagogy.
- Expected: Difficulty is a soft organizer signal. Gemini decides semantic progression and may place a harder prerequisite before an easier application; deterministic code may enforce only trusted source, prerequisite, chain, curriculum, and released-frontier constraints.
- Root cause: The repair treated shared concept identity as proof of semantic interchangeability. In this pipeline, definitions, explanations, examples, and applications for one learning objective normally share that identity, so numeric proximity alone is insufficient evidence for reordering.
- Universal fix and focused retest: Remove the post-Gemini same-concept difficulty repair and its misleading repair telemetry. Gemini still receives the named level plus continuous effective target and explicit closest-band/fill guidance; trusted structural constraints still reconcile its output, and deterministic difficulty ordering remains only the degraded provider-fallback path. An adversarial beginner case now proves Gemini's advanced-difficulty orientation → beginner-difficulty worked example remains unchanged and non-degraded.

### AF-223 — Batch-wide fallback deferral can wait for the full source deadline

- Status: Fixed locally with bounded-latency, stronger-within-window, and no-extra-source regressions; exact-SHA production replay pending
- Severity: Critical — an otherwise valid related last-resort clip can remain private behind a stalled sibling until the shared 210-second source deadline, regressing time-to-first-ready and risking an empty request timeout
- Reproduction: Let one already-started source promptly return a structurally playable Gemini `best_effort` clip while a sibling remains pending. AF-220 correctly defers storage and release so a stronger clip can win, but the deferred clip does not increase `persisted_count`; therefore the existing post-progress idle deadline is never armed and the fallback is considered only after the pending loop reaches its full shared deadline.
- Expected: The fallback remains private during the same bounded post-progress grace window used to await useful inventory. A stronger clip completing inside that window suppresses it. If no stronger clip arrives before the grace expires, pending work is cancelled and the valid fallback is persisted and returned rather than waiting for the full source deadline.
- Root cause: AF-220 separated degraded-lane candidates from persisted stronger inventory, but the pending-source scheduler used only persisted stronger rows as its progress signal. It had no read-only notion of valid deferred surface inventory for deadline and further-acquisition decisions.
- Universal fix and focused retest: The scheduler now counts valid deferred candidates only as available surface inventory, capped by remaining output and persistence capacity; it still does not store, emit, or classify them as stronger progress. Deferred-only progress arms the existing bounded post-progress grace once and later fallback completions cannot extend it, while ordinary stronger inventory preserves its existing threshold. A stronger sibling completing inside the grace remains the sole persisted/emitted row. Cancellation-aware stalled siblings are stopped after the grace and the fallback callback/result arrives well before the patched shared deadline, including when the fallback was the last initial result and the stall belongs to a newly started fourth source. Three completed fallback sources also satisfy a three-reel request without dispatching an unnecessary fourth source. The affected eight-file matrix passes 826 tests and 32 subtests.

### AF-224 — Exact-SHA live output can be relevant yet fail requested breadth and prerequisite progression

- Status: Fixed locally in both organizer-progression and acquisition-coverage halves; exact-SHA deployment and wide production replay pending
- Severity: Critical — the learner receives nonempty, cleanly cut clips, but the feed does not teach the requested curriculum and orders applications before their prerequisite explanations
- Reproduction: After the scoped production reset, submit the structured beginner DC-circuits request on material `9ef5af50-ee8f-476b-857a-02e41f73603d`, job `83217909-0bb5-4a14-b356-69b3055ade52`, generation `5e9f4ab0-2663-4c1a-8753-87e1ce291048`. The authoritative final contains five context-complete, surfaceable `context_aligned` clips, all from video `HsLLq6Rm5tU`, ordered as: solve voltage, solve current, define current, solve resistance, define resistance.
- Expected: Return useful related inventory rather than zero, while preferring enough source/concept breadth to cover the explicit request. The lesson should progress from orientation/definition through explanation to application/worked problem. Missing or imperfect audio/difficulty may be used only as the nonempty last resort.
- Evidence: All five clips have topic relevance `0.80`–`0.85`, informativeness `0.80`–`0.90`, exact persisted/final ranges, two immutable caption cues, and no exact or at-least-80%-overlap duplicate. However, every released row is marked `directly_teaches_topic=false` and `intent_role=supporting`; intent coverage is only `0` or `0.333`. Voltage definition, unit exposition, series circuits, parallel circuits, and their comparison are absent. The organizer is genuine (`lesson_order_v16`, `degraded=false`, provider called) but places worked examples before the corresponding definitions.
- Independent biology control: Fresh material `d6ca7774-44f5-4ce6-8319-2784db1a574a` released four clean, relevant clips from one video in genuinely good purpose → glycolysis → pyruvate transition → oxidative-phosphorylation order, with soft difficulty rising `.2 → .3 → .3 → .4`. It still fails the requested lesson: no actual Krebs-cycle explanation, overall oxygen/CO2/H2O/ATP accounting, oxygen terminal-acceptor role, explicit most-ATP conclusion, comparison, or application. All four rows are again `directly_teaches_topic=false`, `intent_role=supporting`; six usable transcripts yielded only one analyzed source because the others failed provider/audit contracts.
- Root-cause analysis: The first two domains prove the defect is not clip relevance, boundary cutting, local level filtering, exact duplication, or deterministic post-organizer difficulty repair. Candidate/source acquisition repeatedly admits only one source after other relevant transcripts are lost to expensive selector/audit failure, then the release/organizer accepts a supporting-only, obligation-incomplete pool. Organizer ordering itself is not uniformly broken: it follows a coherent source sequence in biology, but lacks enough explicit semantic prerequisite pressure to repair physics's example-first pool. The universal fix must therefore preserve grounded alternate-source candidates before budget exhaustion and make requested coverage/prerequisite sufficiency an organizer/release preference without turning it into a zero-output hard gate.
- Organizer chronology sub-root cause: The organizer prompt, successful-response validator, salvage path, cached-response validator, and degraded fallback all treated every pair of clips from one YouTube source as one inseparable timestamp sequence. That is safe for legacy/context-dependent/overlapping/dependency-linked excerpts, but wrong for the current selector's explicitly self-contained, standalone, nonoverlapping learning units. A valid Gemini plan therefore could not move a later definition ahead of an earlier worked example. The two selector trust booleans were present in persisted `search_context_json` and parsed by ranked feed, but ranked-feed response shaping discarded them before both fresh and prior-unseen candidates reached `order_lesson_batch`.
- Acquisition-coverage sub-root cause: Expansion preserved one forward intent contract but did not require an independent reverse audit of the exact request or an atomic inventory of coordinated tasks, facets, list members, relationship sides, and ordered stages. Downstream acquisition then stopped on scalar reel count alone. It had no trusted expected-obligation set to distinguish five supporting clips from five clips that actually cover the request, and a retry that retained an older database row could incorrectly count the richer incoming clip metadata instead of the metadata actually stored.
- Universal organizer fix: Carry the two current-contract booleans privately through the existing ranked-feed lesson-metadata seam and include them in full and compact organizer payloads. One shared structural predicate now keeps timestamp chronology hard unless every selected same-source unit has the exact current contract, explicit `self_contained=true` and `is_standalone=true`, valid nonoverlapping bounds, and no supplied chain, prerequisite, or trusted curriculum dependency. Only in that fully trusted independent case may Gemini's pedagogical order differ from timestamps; timestamp order remains a deterministic degraded-path tie-break. Missing/legacy/false metadata, overlap, and dependency controls retain the former hard chronology. No transcript/title/concept heuristic, semantic local inference, provider call, query, wait, or sleep was added. Prompt/cache versions advance to `lesson_order_v18`/15.
- Universal acquisition fix: The existing Gemini expansion call now independently audits the request in reverse, declares every coordinated atomic member, and returns the constraint IDs that are genuine source-acquisition obligations. The local schema requires every subject, task, relationship, outcome, and coordinated member while allowing Gemini to exclude purely contextual viewer-level, pacing, tone, and source-format constraints. Only selector-trusted contracts become stable obligation keys. The ingestion scheduler aggregates fulfillment from versioned Gemini-audited metadata on the row actually retained by persistence and, after the current source batch drains, may use another source already inside the existing analysis bound when trusted coverage remains incomplete even though scalar inventory is full. It never rejects, withholds, or delays a valid clip; the exact 75-second post-progress grace is unchanged, complete coverage adds no source/call/sleep, and missing or legacy acquisition contracts preserve the old scalar behavior.
- Focused organizer retest: The exact physics shape now keeps a later current-definition clip before an earlier worked-current clip in one healthy organizer call while a required unseen reel remains present exactly once. A cellular-respiration control preserves purpose → glycolysis → oxygen-role order. Legacy, missing-self-contained, non-standalone, overlapping, chain, prerequisite, and trusted-curriculum cases still repair reverse model output into hard chronology. Full/compact payloads expose the same three trust fields, degraded fallback uses timestamp order without sleeping, fresh ranked rows and recursively recovered prior-unseen rows retain the private flags, and all `151` lesson-ordering tests plus the producer-to-organizer seam controls pass. Exact deployed physics replay remains required together with the separate breadth/acquisition half of AF-224.
- Focused acquisition retest: Physics, biology, math, software, and law requests all preserve atomic reverse coverage and durable acquisition keys under one domain-neutral contract. A malformed coordinated-member omission enters the existing bounded correction path. Contextual beginner/source-format constraints remain in the exact learning contract but not in expected source coverage. An incoming full-coverage clip cannot hide a partial older row retained by candidate identity; only that retained context drives another bounded source start. Complete coverage and contractless legacy inputs start no extra source, a stalled peer under incomplete coverage still stops at the unchanged post-progress grace, and healthy expansion remains one Gemini call with no retry wait. The affected expansion/search/ingestion matrix passes `266` tests and `15` subtests.

### AF-225 — Exact-SHA production generations exceed the no-regression latency guard during provider/contract recovery

- Status: Fixed locally with a bounded, per-candidate Pro recovery contract; exact-SHA deployment and wide production replay pending
- Severity: High — retry succeeds and prevents an empty feed, but the authoritative five-reel release arrives after the agreed streaming-latency guard
- Reproduction: The same DC-circuits job emitted its authoritative final `154.564` seconds after job creation, `21.964` seconds beyond the `132.6`-second guard and `34.8%` above the `115.312`-second baseline.
- Evidence: Durable attempt one received Gemini expansion HTTP 503 `provider_transient`; attempt two succeeded inside the shared maximum of three. Successful work included three Gemini expansion calls, two Pro segmentation calls (`27.887` and `32.486` seconds), and one `1.070`-second organizer call. Retry, terminal, and usage state remained coherent; five provisional rows exactly became the five authoritative rows.
- Biology control: Its authoritative four-reel final arrived in `372.632` seconds, `240.023` seconds beyond the `132.609`-second guard and `223.15%` above baseline. Attempt one spent 14 logical Gemini calls / 16 physical attempts across selection, correction, and recovery; three transcripts produced zero accepted clips before a provider-transient requeue. Attempt two finally admitted four clips from one source.
- Root-cause analysis: Physics begins with a real upstream 503 and later hits AF-226's deterministic counter exception. Biology independently exceeds the guard without AF-226: repeated high-thought Pro selection/repair contracts truncate, time out, or reject valid-source work before a later durable attempt succeeds. The recurring latency is therefore contract-recovery amplification, not a healthy-path sleep or one provider outlier. The universal fix must cap rejected-contract work and retain useful degraded inventory; merely raising duration, attempts, or cost would worsen time-to-first-ready.
- Universal fix: Production remains Gemini Pro proposal followed by Gemini Pro final audit/cutting at medium thinking. Selector and audit structured responses now validate candidates independently. A malformed selector sibling cannot trigger another full-transcript proposal when at least one selector candidate is structurally safe; every survivor still goes through the mandatory Pro audit. A malformed audit sibling cannot discard another candidate that independently passes the complete Pro boundary, direct-start, evidence, objective, intent, relationship, and canonical-family contract. Invalid or unresolved audit items are dropped and selector semantics are never substituted. A source has one shared ceiling of four physical Pro dispatches, corrective calls have no nested transport retry, at least one dispatch remains for the mandatory audit, and provider-success schema/contract correction must begin and finish inside the original 120-second source deadline. Genuine in-call transport recovery retains its existing bounded grace. The healthy path remains exactly two medium Pro calls with no new provider call, search, wait, timer, or sleep.
- Independent cap-audit addendum: A mixed selector sequence could still compose a two-dispatch schema recovery, a one-dispatch correction, a second one-dispatch selector correction, and a one-dispatch audit for five physical Pro dispatches despite the nominal four-dispatch source ceiling. The first root cause was that schema recovery and partial-contract recovery tracked separate logical states; the second was `max(1, remaining)` inventing an audit slot after the selector had spent the source budget. Blocking a second selector correction once any correction has already been consumed and calculating the audit allowance with `max(0, remaining)` closes both compositions. The new regression then exposed a telemetry-integrity defect: the blocked-correction exception retained only the current one-dispatch call and dropped the preceding two-dispatch schema failure, reporting one physical dispatch instead of the actual three. Preserve the complete local selector-call list on that exception. The exact mixed failure now stops before a third selector call or audit, reports physical dispatches `[2, 1]`, and remains below the ceiling; the staged successful recovery still totals exactly four.
- Focused retest: The complete 768-test production selector contract suite and 175-test routing/run/runtime matrix pass; the adjacent Pro output-budget file adds 13 passing controls. Physics, biology, math, software, and law controls retain one fully audited candidate while discarding a malformed sibling in one audit call; raw audit JSON salvages valid items independently; an extra unknown ID no longer poisons a valid expected item; zero-safe responses still receive a bounded correction; a valid selector survivor skips the redundant selector correction but still receives mandatory Pro audit; logical correction cannot start after the original deadline; staged selector-plus-audit recovery totals exactly four Pro dispatches. The settled latency/retry audit adds 83 passing focused checks, including the mixed `[2, 1]` dispatch composition, healthy two-call/no-sleep behavior, retry/deadline accounting, and the shared four-dispatch ceiling. Exact production latency comparison remains required on the deployed SHA.

- Status: Fixed locally with the production `GenerationContext` timeout path; exact-SHA redeploy/replay pending
- Severity: Critical — any source that reaches the bounded post-progress timeout can throw from diagnostics, skip valid completion work, reduce breadth, and turn a planned latency bound into a partial/error path
- Reproduction: In the exact-SHA physics job, `backend/app/ingestion/pipeline.py` calls `context.increment_counter("post_progress_timeouts")` when the 75-second post-progress idle cutoff expires. `GenerationCounter` and `GENERATION_COUNTERS` in `backend/app/clip_engine/provider_runtime.py` omit that key. At `2026-07-23T02:45:09Z`, the production worker therefore raised `ValueError` immediately before the partial final.
- Expected: Expiring the already-bounded grace records one diagnostic count and follows the intended cancellation/fallback completion path. Diagnostics must never change candidate eligibility, persistence, or release behavior.
- Root cause: AF-223 added the counter call with its timeout behavior but did not extend the closed runtime counter contract. Tests asserted timing and output but did not run the production counter validator at that exact seam.

### AF-228 — Explicit recovery resets cost correctly but drops adaptive release lineage

- Status: Fixed locally with separate pedagogical lineage and fresh-provider-budget semantics; exact-SHA redeploy/replay pending
- Severity: Critical — retry keeps the learner’s current feedback weighting but discards prior unseen/frontier, prior coverage, temporal dedupe, and lesson-continuity inputs
- Reproduction: Explicitly retry AF-227’s global provider-budget terminal. One nullable field therefore conflates provider-budget ancestry with pedagogical/release ancestry.
- Universal fix: Only for an explicit global-provider terminal recovery, copy the failed job’s existing pedagogical `source_generation_id` onto the fresh job and persist the existing `fresh_source_budget` entitlement. The failed empty child generation—and therefore its exhausted cost ledger and failed-source attempts—does not become provider-accounting ancestry, while the released parent remains the source for unseen-frontier reconciliation, prior coverage, temporal dedupe, and lesson continuity. Root global failures remain roots, and ordinary empty-exhausted retries retain their prior reset behavior.

The explicit retry starts with attempt zero, empty usage, zero Gemini ledger exposure, the full three-source budget, the unchanged adaptation fingerprint, and the parent generation as both job and generated-row lineage. Repeating the request coalesces to the same queued job. The organizer receives the unseen reel exactly once as required, receives both parent releases as prior coverage, excludes a fresh temporal overlap with the unseen source clip, and persists the unseen ID exactly once in reconciliation and authoritative chain output. The new regression plus adjacent global, failed-continuation, ordinary exhausted, retryable-source, and coalescing controls pass `11 passed`; the complete generation API/jobs suites pass `284 passed`.

### AF-230 — Organizer releases overlong, semantically repetitive clips instead of a concise atomic reel lesson

- Status: Fixed locally with a universal soft cadence/nonredundancy organizer contract; exact-SHA redeploy/replay pending
- Severity: High — clips are relevant and boundary-clean, but multi-minute segments break reel cadence, repeat the same explanation, and consume lesson positions without satisfying the missing formal objective
- Reproduction: Fresh derivatives material `65f2e2d6-b016-431e-8c02-b12e966605d5`, job `0681f7b5…`, generation `2a833b6b…`, authoritatively releases clips of `52.04`, `183.87`, `103.05`, `74.08`, and `28.27` seconds. The 183.87-second clip repeatedly moves a secant point toward a limit and explicitly stops before formal limits; the 103.05-second clip repeats average-to-instantaneous rate via shrinking time intervals.
- Expected: Prefer concise, atomic, self-contained clips and complementary concepts. A long or semantically repetitive but valid related clip remains eligible only as a last-resort nonempty fallback when no concise/nonredundant alternative exists.
- Evidence: Every cut is `context_aligned`, caption-grounded, standalone/self-contained, and starts/ends on complete thoughts; this is not a boundary-integrity failure. The genuine `lesson_order_v16` organizer releases the 183.87-second clip at rank 2 and the semantically near-duplicate 103.05-second clip at rank 3. The feed still omits the formal difference quotient and its derivation, while all five released rows remain honest `supporting` clips.
- Root cause: The selector correctly treats an indivisible explanation, derivation, proof, problem, mechanism, or chain as valid at any length, and the generated-reel duration request is intentionally inert; therefore the 183.87-second complete interval is expected selector output, not a boundary or off-by-one defect. Selector dedupe is source-local, so it cannot compare the 183.87-second and 103.05-second explanations from different videos. The cross-source Gemini organizer is the correct semantic authority, but `lesson_order_v16` received only start/end timestamps, described duration only as a reason not to omit a unique clip, and did not say that `release_limit` was a ceiling rather than a target or require a final pairwise redundancy audit. Selecting all five therefore passed every structural validator. The absent formal difference quotient is a separate upstream inventory-coverage limitation: the organizer can prefer complementary supplied content but cannot invent a missing clip.
- Universal fix: `lesson_order_v17` sends the exact selected interval length as `clip_duration_seconds` in both full and compact payloads and makes cadence explicitly soft. It asks the same existing Gemini call for the smallest coherent set, treats `release_limit` as a ceiling, audits every optional selected pair across source/title/concept differences, keeps the shortest context-complete equivalent, and records omitted equivalents in `current_restatement_reel_ids`. A longer clip still wins when it uniquely supplies required setup, reasoning, conclusion, remediation, application, or another requested facet; required unseen clips remain mandatory; an all-repeat or only-long/best-effort pool must still return at least one valid related clip. The selector, boundaries, acquisition, local eligibility, and fallback ordering are unchanged. Cache/prompt versions advance together, with no duration threshold, topic/domain branch, lexical/embedding duplicate heuristic, provider call, retry, query, wait, or sleep.
- Focused retest: The complete lesson-ordering suite passes `140` tests. New coverage exposes exact full/compact duration even when a stale stored duration disagrees with timestamps; exercises paraphrased cross-source repeats plus distinct applications across derivatives, cellular respiration, electric circuits, Python exceptions, and negligence; proves the healthy path dispatches exactly once and never sleeps; preserves the distinct contribution; and proves a provider failure still returns the sole 260-second `best_effort` related proof nonempty. Existing 128-candidate prompt-budget, dependency, required-unseen, semantic-restatement, unique long-content, cache, and fallback controls remain green.

### AF-231 — Rate-limited adaptive generation exhausts every durable attempt in three seconds

- Status: Fixed locally with typed provider retry hints and bounded failure-only durable backoff; exact-SHA deployment replay pending
- Severity: Critical — quiz adaptation is calculated correctly, but retries fire so quickly that a transient provider quota window produces zero reels before it has any chance to recover
- Reproduction: Answer the math recall check for reel `ingest-870c…` / concept “polynomial derivative example” incorrectly. Assessment session `979e3a8a…` completes at `0/1`; the exact concept adjustment and material global adjustment become `-0.12`, revision advances to one, and adaptive job `655102ae-be13-4d64-8a30-cc4c868f295c`, generation `b138cd97-e3d7-4af1-90e7-c5e77287ab0d`, starts with effective target `.03`, new fingerprint `43aa65…`, correct parent lineage, and both prior source videos excluded.
- Expected: A wrong answer increases/remediates that concept in newly generated child reels. A 429 response retries within the shared three-to-five-attempt ceiling using provider `Retry-After` or bounded failure-only backoff; healthy calls remain immediate and receive no new wait.
- Evidence: The adaptive job issues nine expansion dispatches: each of three durable attempts immediately tries two Flash-Lite calls plus one 3.6 fallback. All nine receive HTTP 429. The complete job terminates `provider_rate_limited` after only `3.058` seconds with zero videos, transcripts, candidates, or authoritative final. Known billed cost remains zero.
- Independent software control: Fresh Python-exceptions job `ff25a6ae-771c-4479-b561-5f2676a967fd` repeats the identical provider-throttle pattern outside adaptation: nine expansion dispatches across three durable attempts all receive HTTP 429, and the job fails after `2.839` seconds with zero discovery, transcripts, candidates, or final. This proves the defect is universal retry timing rather than topic or quiz logic.
- Root cause: Durable retry classification is correct, but the requeue path provides essentially no rate-limit recovery window. Model fallback cannot help while the provider-level quota window is shared, so the current rapid fan-out multiplies identical 429s and consumes the entire bounded attempt count.
- Provider-hint audit: These responses persist only status `429` / `ClientError`; neither provider metadata, terminal payload, nor Railway logs contain `Retry-After`, `retryDelay`, quota metric, or raw headers. A safe default delay is therefore required. Google's current Gemini troubleshooting guidance recommends transient-only exponential backoff beginning around one second, increasing on later attempts, with a fixed maximum and jitter.
- Universal fix and focused retest: Gemini telemetry now carries a typed, bounded `retry_after_sec` hint through the same durable usage ledger. Rate-limited requeues honor that hint; when none exists, attempt one waits five seconds and attempt two waits fifteen seconds before the next lease. Non-rate-limit transient failures remain immediate, the three-attempt ceiling is unchanged, and healthy calls add no delay or provider call. Fake-clock job regressions prove both default windows, hint precedence, no early lease, and the zero-delay non-rate-limit control; typed HTTP 429 mapping and the wider focused generation matrix pass.

### Release constraint — healthy-path reel streaming latency

- Requirement: These fixes must not increase time-to-first-ready or subsequent reel streaming cadence on successful requests.
- Guardrail: Healthy provider/database paths remain one physical attempt with no added sleeps; retries run only after a recoverable failure inside the background worker, and already-ready reels remain visible while later work retries.
- Pre-deployment baseline: On deployed revision `2774a76`, clean Newton job `15584162-e4a5-4108-93e8-7bdfb9f3ec13` was created at `19:11:49.668260Z` and emitted its seven-reel final event at `19:13:44.980606Z`: 115.312 seconds from job creation (115.254 seconds from worker start). This revision emits no earlier partial reel event for that job.
- Verification: Pending the identical Newton request on the exact new deployed revision, comparing job creation/start to first reel-bearing event and terminal batch cadence.

### AF-232 — Pro-quality segmentation repeats expensive full-transcript work

- Status: Reverted at the user's request. The original medium-thinking Pro selector plus medium-thinking Pro full-transcript final audit is restored.
- Reproduction: The production source pass used a medium-thinking Pro selector and then a second medium-thinking Pro audit over the full transcript. Transport, schema, selector-contract, audit-schema, and audit-contract retries each had separate opportunities to spend again. A partly malformed audit response also discarded independently valid Pro decisions.
- Reversion decision: Quality authority stays with Gemini Pro for both candidate proposal and cutting/audit. The experimental low-thinking Flash proposal, proposal-local transcript windows, Flash-proposal partial-audit salvage, cost-test contract, cache-version bump, and exact Flash pricing additions were removed together. AF-225's later Pro-only retention of independently complete audited siblings remains a separate quality-preserving recovery path.
- Root cause: The selector and auditor duplicated high-rate semantic work, the audit resent the whole transcript instead of proposal-local context, and stage-local retry budgets multiplied cost. Audit parsing was all-or-nothing, while the initial degraded fallback incorrectly treated a Pro-grounded boundary with invalid Pro semantics as safe and could therefore surface Flash-authored concept metadata.
- Verification required after reversion: routing, selector, audit, cache, production-run, captionless-source, retry, and healthy-path latency tests must prove the restored two-Pro behavior and no remaining Flash-proposal production route.
- Reversion regression caught: The first focused run passed 951 checks and caught one test-only assertion accidentally restored to cache contract `quality_silence_v40`. Production correctly retained the earlier AF-230 `quality_silence_v41` contract; the assertion was repaired before rerunning the matrix.
- Completed reversion retest: The repaired routing, selector, audit, cache, production-run, captionless-source, retry, and provider-runtime matrix passes all 952 checks. An independent audit also passes 27 targeted Pro-routing, retry, contract-preservation, and deadline assertions and finds no AF-232 production residue. The low-level direct/evaluation selector default remains its pre-existing Flash route, but both production entrypoints explicitly force medium-thinking `pro_only` selection and disable Flash failover.

### AF-233 — Full-suite cache assertion retained the reverted experimental namespace

- Status: Fixed locally; exact-SHA deployment and live replay pending
- Severity: Release-gate only — production behavior was already correct, but the stale expectation made the complete backend suite fail
- Reproduction: `backend/tests/clip_engine/test_segment_cache.py::test_segment_cache_key_tracks_transcript_topic_and_policy` expected `quality_silence_v41:v39`, while production returned `quality_silence_v41:v38`.
- Root cause: AF-232 intentionally removed its experimental segment-cache version bump while retaining AF-230's current `quality_silence_v41` selection contract. One combined test expectation retained the reverted `v39` half after the focused reversion matrix.
- Fix and exact retest: Restore only the assertion to `quality_silence_v41:v38`. This changes no runtime key, cache read, provider call, retry, wait, or latency path. The exact focused reproduction passes, and the complete backend rerun passes `3,108` tests with one skipped test and `65` subtests. The final post-AF-225/AF-227 release suite remains a separate gate.

### AF-234 — Two Pro-output budget mocks bypassed Gemini's compact wire schema

- Status: Fixed locally; focused and final complete-suite gates pass, exact-SHA deployment pending
- Severity: Release-gate only — the production parser correctly enforced the compact Gemini audit contract, but two output-budget tests supplied an impossible mock shape
- Reproduction: The post-AF-225/AF-227 full backend/pipeline gate passed `3,792` tests and failed only `test_text_only_pro_keeps_candidate_budget_after_observed_thought_usage` and `test_text_only_pro_retries_one_malformed_structured_response`. Their mocked audit response used `model_dump_json()` and therefore emitted internal Python field names; the live response schema exposes compact aliases such as `t`, `f`, `family`, `ie`, `oi`, `rw`, and `ow`.
- Root cause and fix: Per-item audit parsing now intentionally requires the exact live wire fields before independently salvaging a candidate. Change only those two mocks to `model_dump_json(by_alias=True)`, matching the neighboring production-shaped fixtures and real Gemini schema. The malformed-selector control also expected the old nested transport retry on its logical correction; update that assertion from one to zero because AF-225 deliberately makes correction calls single-dispatch. No production parser, provider call, token budget, retry, wait, or latency path changes.
- Final retest: The focused selector/routing/output/run/runtime matrix passes `956` tests. The authoritative backend and pipeline command passes `3,794` tests with one intentional skip and all `65` subtests; the only three warnings are pre-existing SWIG import deprecations.

### AF-235 — Text/file retrieval drops the extracted AI concept summary before Gemini expansion and Pro clipping

- Status: Fixed locally with a bounded universal handoff; exact-SHA deployment and live five-domain replay pending
- Severity: Critical — the uploaded material is analyzed by Gemini, but downstream search and clip selection can operate on only a short concept title, losing the explanatory context that disambiguates what the learner actually supplied
- Reproduction: Material Intelligence returns and persists each concept's title, keywords, and summary. The deep generation path selects a concept but normally builds the clip-engine request from the clean title alone. Gemini query expansion therefore compresses and expands that title, and its `corrected` value becomes the Pro selector topic; neither provider is guaranteed to receive the already-extracted concept summary.
- Expected: Without adding a provider call or delaying the healthy path, the existing AI-derived, persisted concept context should travel into the cached Gemini expansion request and then into the Gemini Pro transcript selector/auditor. Topic-only requests must retain their current literal behavior, and exact intent must not broaden.
- Root cause: The material-analysis and clip-acquisition stages persist compatible semantic fields but the `_concept_topic_query` handoff uses the concept label as the downstream learning request. The retrieval contract is therefore narrower than the material-intelligence result.
- Universal fix: Keep the persisted concept title as the exact request and trusted intent identity, but carry its normalized summary as an optional 600-character `source_context` through `ReelService`, ingestion, initial search, zero-search recovery, and zero-valid-clip recovery. The existing Gemini expansion prompt may use that backend-authored context only to disambiguate the title and produce a concrete, source-grounded `corrected` learning intent; it cannot create exact-request constraints or mandatory scope from context alone. The normalized context participates in the expansion cache identity. The resulting `corrected` value already feeds the existing medium-thinking Gemini Pro selector/auditor, so this adds no model call, search, wait, timer, or sleep. Topic-only materials send no context and retain the old prompt/cache shape. Recovery now remains on the selected concept query instead of replacing it with the broader material subject. The generic synthetic `Learning Objectives` pseudo-concept was removed because searching that label discarded the actual objective.
- Focused retest: Physics, biology, math, software, and law summaries all cross the same handoff while preserving exact titles and one-call expansion. Blank/omitted context retains the prior cache identity; differently grounded summaries do not collide. Both zero-result and zero-valid-clip recovery keep the narrow concept and identical context despite a broader literal material topic, and recursive ingestion preserves it. The Gemini prompt contains one clearly delimited context block while the exact request remains authoritative. Existing pipeline coverage proves the expansion's `corrected` intent reaches Pro segmentation. The affected nine-file matrix passes `567` tests, one intentional skip, and `15` subtests.

### AF-236 — Failed material-intelligence responses can be cached as successful empty payloads

- Status: Fixed locally with a three-dispatch hard ceiling and success-only cache; exact-SHA deployment pending
- Severity: High — one transient concept/objective extraction failure can permanently pin that exact material/model/prompt hash to deterministic fallback instead of allowing a later AI recovery
- Reproduction: `_generate_payload` converts every provider or JSON error to `{}`. `_cached_or_generate` unconditionally writes that payload into `llm_cache`, whose read path has no freshness check.
- Expected: A healthy call remains one call and cached success remains reusable. A failed/empty AI response must not become an indefinite success cache entry; bounded retry must respect the existing request latency envelope and deterministic fallback must remain available.
- Root cause: The cache layer cannot distinguish a validated empty curriculum result from the failure sentinel returned by the provider layer.
- Universal fix: A material-analysis result is cacheable only when it contains at least one concept with both a nonblank title and the source-grounded summary required by AF-235. Empty, malformed, objectives-only, title-only, corrupt, and legacy null cache values are ignored. Provider generation makes at most three total attempts and stores only the first usable result; exhaustion returns the existing deterministic fallback without writing a failure sentinel, so a later request may recover. The configured Gemini model is now actually passed to the router. Material analysis limits each outer attempt to one credential slot, and the Gemini SDK client explicitly sets `HttpRetryOptions(attempts=1)`, making three outer attempts a hard maximum of three physical Gemini dispatches rather than multiplying hidden transport retries. Healthy success remains one dispatch.
- Focused retest: Empty and incomplete responses recover on a later attempt; attempt four never runs; all calls use the configured model and one-key limit. Three failed attempts write no successful cache, an existing `{}` is ignored, a later complete result replaces it, and the subsequent request is a cache hit. A non-string legacy cache value is ignored instead of aborting material creation. The shared router test proves a rate-limited credential consumes one physical dispatch, rotates once, and lets the next bounded outer attempt use the healthy key with SDK retry count one.

### AF-237 — Global whitespace normalization erases document line structure before deterministic heading fallback

- Status: Fixed locally without changing stored/chunk identity; exact-SHA deployment pending
- Severity: Medium — when AI material analysis is unavailable, valid Markdown, text, PDF, or DOCX headings can no longer be detected because all line breaks have already been collapsed
- Reproduction: File/text/topic parts are joined and immediately passed through `normalize_whitespace`, which replaces every whitespace run, including newlines, with a single space. `headings_from_text` later calls `splitlines`, but receives a one-line string.
- Expected: Stable normalized text and chunk identity remain deterministic while the fallback extractor retains enough source structure to recognize headings. No extra provider call, search, wait, or clip-streaming delay should be added.
- Root cause: One normalized representation is reused both for persistence/chunking and for structure-aware fallback extraction even though those consumers require different whitespace semantics.
- Universal fix and focused retest: Material creation now retains a structured joined representation only for concept/objective analysis while continuing to derive validation, chunks, embeddings, persistence, idempotency behavior, and `materials.raw_text` from the same normalized representation as before. An API regression proves multiline text plus topic reaches analysis with its line breaks intact while the stored material and chunk remain deterministically flattened. Deterministic fallback recognizes representative physics, biology, math, software, and law headings through the same domain-neutral code.
- Final AF-235 through AF-237 local gates: The authoritative backend/pipeline collection passes `3,805` tests, one intentional skip, and `75` subtests. The deployed Next frontend passes all `216` tests, TypeScript validation, and the production build. The explicit healthy/recovery latency guard passes `19` checks in `1.70` seconds: material analysis is one dispatch when healthy and at most three on failure; expansion is one call with no retry wait; Gemini transport has no hidden healthy retry; the organizer remains one call; selector plus mandatory Pro audit remains exactly two healthy calls; mixed corrective compositions stay inside their shared dispatch ceilings; and the existing post-progress timeout remains bounded.

### AF-238 — The backend-added subject hint becomes a fake heading concept

- Status: Fixed locally during independent final audit; exact-SHA deployment pending
- Severity: High — a text/file material with a capitalized subject can acquire and search a synthetic concept such as `Topic: Biology` instead of a concept actually present in the learner's material
- Reproduction: Preserve line structure for AF-237, submit text plus `subject_tag=Biology`, and run deterministic heading fallback while material AI is unavailable. The backend-created `Topic: Biology` line is title-cased, so `headings_from_text` accepts the entire transport label as a heading.
- Root cause: The source representation combined user-authored file/text content with the backend-authored topic hint before structure-aware analysis. The hint is useful for normalized persistence and topic-only identity, but `subject_tag` is already passed to Material Intelligence separately.
- Universal fix and focused retest: Maintain a separate structured analysis representation containing only user file/text content. Continue appending the topic hint to normalized validation, chunks, embeddings, persistence, and idempotent material identity. When there is no file/text content, use the full representation so topic-only materials keep their deterministic root seed. The API regression uses capitalized `Biology`, proves analysis receives only the multiline user text, and proves stored/chunk text still ends in normalized `Topic: Biology`; the existing topic-only controls remain unchanged.

### AF-239 — Material retry hardening accidentally changes every shared Gemini text caller

- Status: Fixed locally during independent final audit; exact-SHA deployment pending

Material analysis still passes `gemini_key_attempt_limit=1`, so its three outer attempts remain a hard three physical Gemini dispatches. Ordinary shared text calls construct the same client shape as before. Complementary router tests fail if the ordinary path receives the override or if the bounded path omits it.

### AF-240 — A new valid search can be stranded with no job while an earlier continuation is active

- Status: Fixed locally; exact production retest pending
- Severity: Critical — the material is durably created, but the user receives a terminal-looking empty feed and no background work exists that could ever populate it
- Production reproduction (2026-07-23, immediately after the guarded clean-state reset): Start biology material `82089a77-4f0c-4745-a1a9-d3a642331e61`. While its automatic continuation job `039c41a5-5a31-42b1-b184-49109078e914` is the learner's only active job, submit math material `0cc2d3bb-4868-4a30-bc29-c84ec5b13db6`, then software material `4da17a18-4590-4513-9307-eff61518643b`.
- Evidence: Both later materials persist successfully, but neither receives any `reel_generation_jobs` row. The software feed renders `Generation is busy. Retry after an active request finishes.`, `No reels yet`, and a manual `Retry` button. The same read-only query finds exactly one active job globally for Asplarity: the biology continuation.
- Expected: A valid, authenticated new material must converge to a generation job without relying on the learner to remain on the empty feed and press Retry at the right time. Capacity control may delay execution, but it must not silently convert a valid search into a permanently jobless material. Recovery must preserve idempotency, avoid duplicate jobs, and add no work or delay to the healthy no-contention path.
- Root cause: API submission passed a global active-job ceiling of four and a per-learner ceiling of one into the durable job repository. Because queued and running jobs both counted, the biology continuation reached the learner ceiling. The rejection occurred before `before_create` and before insertion; feed autofill then suppressed that capacity `429`, so the new material had no job to resume. The frontend performed no autonomous capacity retry. Separately, unleased jobs were failed after eight minutes and the browser counted queued time against its execution timeout, so simply allowing a deeper queue would still have lost valid work under sustained load.
- Universal fix: Authenticated API and feed-autofill submissions now persist an idempotent durable queued job after the existing verified-account, six-per-minute burst, billing, and quota checks. The existing single worker still bounds provider concurrency and cost. API jobs carry an internal durable-queue marker, so they do not expire before their first lease; their one-hour execution deadline is reset when processing actually starts. Legacy repository callers may still opt into the old active ceilings and queue TTL. The browser likewise starts its finite execution timeout only after the job runs, attempts, or emits its first event. The no-contention path adds no provider call, sleep, or database round trip.
- Focused regression: Backend tests now prove a distinct request is queued behind existing same-learner work, repeated submissions coalesce to one job, billing reservation runs once per created job, feed autofill returns the queued job ID, a marked job leases after the legacy TTL with a fresh deadline, and unmarked stale jobs still fail once. Frontend stream tests advance the clock beyond the old 69-minute limit while a job remains unattempted, then prove it completes after running; they also prove a queued retry with an attempt retains a finite execution timeout.

### AF-241 — Live batches can stop with relevant introductory clips but omit requested application objectives

- Status: Universal objective-acquisition and continuation fixes complete locally; exact production retest pending
- Severity: High — returned clips are individually relevant and context-aligned, but the lesson does not cover enough of the user's explicit request to achieve the learning objective
- Production reproduction: Biology material `82089a77-4f0c-4745-a1a9-d3a642331e61` requested helicase, primase, polymerase, leading/lagging strands, Okazaki fragments, proofreading, and what happens when an error escapes repair. Its four released clips cover the replication mechanism but contain no proofreading, mutation, or repair explanation. Software material `4da17a18-4590-4513-9307-eff61518643b` requested the URL-to-page path through DNS, TCP, TLS, HTTP, server handling, status codes, caching, and a 404-versus-500 debugging comparison. Its five released clips cover URL structure, DNS, and TLS, but omit TCP, HTTP/server handling, status codes, caching, and the debugging comparison.
- Evidence: Every released software clip is marked self-contained with a `context_aligned` boundary and has a valid concept family, so this is not a start/end or unrelated-video failure. The final continuation exhausted after a three-second inventory pass even though multiple explicit requested objectives remained uncovered.
- Expected: The organizer may return any number of clips, but a batch should continue acquiring universally relevant candidates for uncovered high-priority objectives before declaring inventory exhausted. It must still prefer returning a valid related fallback over an empty result, without fabricating coverage or imposing a topic-specific clip count.
- Root-cause evidence: The cached Gemini expansion is not missing the user's intent: it contains 10 biology obligations and 13 software obligations. Supadata returned seven proofreading/repair candidates and twenty 404/500 candidates. None reached source analysis. Ranked source selection limits its obligation-family diversity search to the first `2 × analysis_prefix` globally ranked rows, so strong broad-query videos can fill that narrow window while lower-view results from an uncovered explicit-objective query remain invisible. Continuations also do not carry chain-wide fulfilled/uncovered obligations back into acquisition. In the software chain, the second job left two private DNS clips; because any raw parent inventory existed, the third job set its fresh source budget to zero. The organizer then removed the remaining DNS restatement, and the job terminalized `exhausted` without searching for the uncovered HTTP/status/debugging objectives.
- Universal fix: Expansion cache v15 preserves each selector-validated Gemini query's exact `preserved_constraint_ids`, derives its stable intent-obligation keys only after the full request contract passes the existing trust gate, and carries those annotations through Supadata result sets and merged source ranking. The bounded analysis prefix now reserves its existing source slots for distinct focused objective branches—including on a fresh chain—and subtracts chain-wide obligation keys already fulfilled by authoritative releases on continuations. This changes neither search/segmentation budgets nor provider-call count. When a cached-only continuation is admitted as related but the organizer excludes every current candidate as a same-adaptation restatement, the generation records that exact editorial omission as an empty nonterminal partial checkpoint. The existing bounded zero-growth client loop immediately requests the next continuation; its restatement guard removes the rejected cache rows, so that pass receives the normal fresh source budget instead of falsely terminalizing.
- Focused retest: Cache round-trip tests preserve query/constraint/obligation metadata; parameterized biology and software rankings surface a distant focused objective both on a fresh chain and after a frequent objective is covered; deep discovery carries only trusted annotations into ranking; and the exact two-continuation regression proves the first cached-restatement pass performs no retrieval, returns a continuation-bearing partial, then the next pass excludes the restatement, receives the full bounded source budget plus prior fulfilled keys, and releases a fresh objective. Existing frontend startup/refill loops prove zero-growth partials continue automatically with a hard three-attempt bound. AF-241 focused and integration gates pass 451 tests plus 15 subtests, with syntax and scoped diff checks clean.

Consequently the organizer accepted kinetic-energy material before gravitational-potential-energy material despite a persisted GPE-before-KE curriculum edge.

### AF-243 — Context-dependent or entertainment-tailed ranges can be mislabeled self-contained

- Status: Universal AI-only fix complete locally; exact production retest pending
- Severity: High — the clip is related, but the user can enter after required setup or remain through a long non-teaching tail
- Production reproduction: In physics material `c34d99a5-3524-406b-8866-b59fa3cbf459`, the released free-fall clip begins with the conclusion “When we add together, at every point along the curve…” and uses an unexplained prior table and `70.6 joules`, yet is labeled `self_contained=true` and `is_standalone=true`. A 119.2-second pendulum clip continues through countdown, suspense, screaming, and laughter after the educational explanation has ended. A second pendulum range relies on the setup from the preceding clip while also being labeled standalone.
- Evidence: All nine physics releases are persisted as `context_aligned` with verified speech corridors, but none has direct acoustic verification because YouTube audio retrieval hit the bot challenge. Transcript edges are grammatically complete for most clips, so sentence completeness alone is not detecting discourse dependence or a long non-instructional tail.
- Expected: Gemini must reject or expand a range whose opening depends on prior visual/data/discourse context, and must stop a range when the learning unit closes rather than carrying entertainment reactions. When acoustic evidence is unavailable, transcript/word evidence may provide a valid related fallback, but `self_contained` and `standalone` must remain semantically truthful. The fix must work across arbitrary subjects and must not require local Whisper.
- Root cause: The Gemini Pro selector emits `self_contained` and `is_standalone`, but the existing mandatory final Pro boundary audit can repair or replace the selected start/end without returning either field. The repaired final span therefore inherits stale selector booleans even though its semantic independence may differ. Downstream `context_aligned` validation proves only that the timestamps match a permitted speech corridor; exact transcript anchors and word-edge checks likewise cannot decide whether an opening depends on an omitted table, quantity, referent, visual setup, or whether a complete lesson has already ended before a reaction/performance tail. The smallest universal correction is to have the existing audit call judge both booleans for the exact final span using its adjacent transcript context and persist those final judgments. This adds no model call, heuristic content matcher, local transcription, or healthy-path wait.
- Universal fix and focused retest: Pro audit contract v13 makes compact `self` and `stand` required judgments for the final repaired `sq`→`eq` speech, shows the auditor that exact selected span plus adjacent transcript cues, and explicitly requires cold-viewer checks for unresolved referents, inherited quantities/givens, indispensable visuals, and the earliest complete educational stop before performance or reaction tails. The audited booleans replace the selector's stale values when the repaired topic is propagated. A false value remains truthful fallback metadata and never becomes a new rejection gate. Biology proves a dependent conclusion opening changes stale true/true to false; chemistry proves reaction-tail trimming and a clean independent unit retaining true; schema tests require both fields; forty-candidate output remains within the existing cap; and the healthy path remains exactly one selector plus one audit. The full selector contract passes 772 tests, while the output-budget, provider-schema, and healthy-call controls pass 17.

### AF-244 — A durable queued generation can outlive and silently lose its quota reservation

- Status: Fixed locally across current and legacy reservation links; exact production retest pending
- Severity: High — a job may remain validly queued, receive an automatic quota refund after two hours, then execute later without a live reservation, so daily-search accounting no longer reflects accepted work
- Reproduction: Submit a generation job carrying the new durable attempt-zero queue marker, attach its `reserved` search-quota row, keep the worker occupied past the billing reconciler's two-hour stale threshold, then trigger any billing-status/reservation operation. The job remains `queued` by design, while `reconcile_stale_reservations` selects the old reservation solely by `usage_day`/`updated_at` and refunds it.
- Expected: A reservation attached to any nonterminal queued/running generation remains reserved until that job reaches a terminal settlement. Only genuinely orphaned stale reservations may be age-refunded. This must not change healthy submission, queue leasing, provider concurrency, or reel-stream latency.
- Root cause: AF-240 deliberately decouples legitimate queue wait from the old eight-minute queue TTL, but the billing stale reconciler still assumes every reservation older than two hours has exceeded the maximum job lifetime. It does not inspect either the many-to-many reservation/job link or the legacy direct job link before refunding. The result is a cross-contract lifetime mismatch, not a provider or subscription-tier failure.
- Universal fix and focused retest: Stale reconciliation now excludes a reservation whenever either the current junction table or the legacy direct job field links it to any queued/running generation. Orphan age/day rollover refunds remain unchanged, and the existing terminal transition still consumes a usable completion or refunds a failed empty result. An eight-case matrix covers junction/legacy linkage, queued/running state, and both two-hour age and UTC-day staleness; a separate orphan control still refunds. The full billing file passes 60 tests, generation-job repository passes 48, and five selected durable-queue/terminal API controls pass.

### AF-245 — The final audit can persist `standalone=true` while `self_contained=false`

- Status: Fixed locally with a no-retry structural invariant; exact production retest pending
- Severity: Medium — the organizer and adaptive feed receive contradictory truth metadata from one otherwise valid related clip

### AF-247 — Restatement-only continuations can emit successive empty partial checkpoints

- Status: Fixed locally with one checkpoint, strongest-valid fallback, and independently verified metadata invariants; exact production retest pending
- Severity: High — the client has a bounded zero-growth loop, but the backend chain itself has no same-adaptation editorial-reacquisition ceiling and can keep producing empty nonterminal batches
- Reproduction: First cached continuation is fully omitted as a current restatement and records an empty partial. The next fresh acquisition is valid/related but the organizer again omits every current candidate as a restatement while retaining a prior required guard. The current condition records another empty partial.
- Expected: One empty editorial checkpoint may unlock a fresh bounded search. If that search again yields only a valid related restatement, release the strongest current candidate as the required last-resort fallback rather than returning another empty batch. Preserve exact duplicate/source exclusions and the watched/unseen prefix.
- Root cause: Editorial reacquisition checks only the current organizer result and does not inspect whether the same-adaptation source chain already contains a restatement checkpoint.
- Independent post-fix finding: The first implementation could mark an empty checkpoint when only some current candidates were identified as restatements, so an unexplained organizer omission could incorrectly consume the one allowed reacquisition. It also injected the fallback after computing the cross-batch unseen reconciliation tail; the tail then omitted the newly ordered fallback ID and failed its own persisted subset contract. Tighten both checkpoint and fallback qualification to a continuation with a nonempty adaptation, nonempty selected guard, and every current candidate explicitly classified as a restatement. When the fallback is appended after the preserved unseen prefix, append it to any reconciliation tail in the same canonical order while keeping only the organizer-selected rows as guards for any still-omitted candidates.
- Universal fix and focused retest: The same-adaptation chain stores one explicit editorial checkpoint. A second fully classified restatement-only omission releases rank zero from the already-filtered current candidate pool, removes only that released ID from omission metadata, preserves the prior unseen prefix and organizer-only guards, appends the fallback to any reconciliation tail, and marks the release degraded without another provider or organizer call. Matching versus changed adaptation, multiple ranked candidates, strongest-only release, exactly one checkpoint, and a third continuation are covered. The complete generation-job API file passes all 240 tests, and an independent seven-test terminal/continuation matrix passes.

Original cursor and recovery rows keep distinct constraint/objective keys and provenance.
