### AF-250 — A one-slot analysis prefix can displace the literal anchor

- Status: Fixed locally across zero/one/multi-slot literal and adaptive matrices; exact production retest pending
- Severity: High — when only one segmentation slot remains, the one source actually analyzed can become an expanded-query branch instead of the highest-ranked literal anchor, or can repeat an already-covered AI objective instead of the available uncovered branch
- Reproduction: Rank one short literal source followed by two short AI-expanded sources, then select with `limit=3` and `analysis_prefix=1`. The forced diversity reserve is one, so the literal prefix slice is empty and a nonliteral source is inserted first. Separately, with no literal source, mark the leading AI rows as a covered objective and a lower short row as uncovered; the unconditional one-row initial selection fills the sole prefix before objective reservation runs.
- Expected: A positive prefix with a literal anchor always keeps at least one literal slot. Without a literal anchor, a sole slot should select the strongest short candidate for an uncovered trusted objective before repeating a covered objective. An explicitly zero prefix must not be silently coerced to one or reorder the ranked tail. Objective diversity may use only genuinely remaining fixed slots and must never add a source or provider call.
- Root cause: `reserve` is clamped to at least one while the literal-anchor slice uses `prefix_limit - reserve` without its own minimum; the no-literal path fills one slot before considering uncovered objective candidates; and the prefix calculation coerces an explicit zero to one.
- Universal fix and focused retest: An explicit zero prefix preserves ranked order. A one-slot literal pool pins the literal anchor; a one-slot AI-only pool prefers an uncovered objective over a covered repeat; larger pools pin one literal anchor and fill distinct objectives before repetition. Prefix zero through three, `limit=1`, covered/uncovered feedback, and all-literal `A,A,A,B,C` controls pass without changing provider or analysis counts.

### AF-251 — An unused recovery expansion can overwrite the contract for original-cursor results

- Status: Fixed locally by keeping the initial validated intent contract canonical; exact production retest pending
- Severity: Critical — downstream ingestion can attach the wrong corrected intent and obligation contract to a source even though its per-query provenance is accurate
- Reproduction: Initial Gemini search returns zero videos with an open original-query cursor. Prepare a recovery expansion, then let the original cursor supply enough inventory before any recovery query is dispatched. The response lists only the original query and its original objective metadata, but top-level `corrected`, `intent_contract`, and acquisition obligations come from the unused recovery expansion.
- Expected: Accumulated query metadata may be retained before pagination, but the initial validated response-level corrected intent and contract stay canonical for the discovery invocation. Recovery is an acquisition-query plan, not permission to relabel the learner's exact intent.
- Root cause: The mutable top-level `expansion` is assigned to the recovery plan when recovery queries are merely prepared, before `_continue_provider_pages` decides whether an existing cursor already satisfies the fixed analysis target.
- Universal fix and focused retest: Recovery never replaces the invocation's canonical corrected summary, intent contract, or acquisition IDs. Original-cursor success makes no recovery call; a genuinely dispatched recovery contributes only attempted queries and independently retained query metadata/provenance.

### AF-252 — Recovery Gemini is called before usable existing provider cursors

- Status: Fixed locally with cursor-first lazy recovery; exact production latency/cost retest pending
- Severity: High — a redundant model call adds cost and time-to-first-reel, and its failure can prevent retrieval of a valid already-issued YouTube cursor
- Reproduction: The initial validated expansion/search returns zero videos plus a page-two cursor. Configure page two to return a valid short related source, then make recovery expansion raise. Discovery raises before page two is requested. When recovery expansion succeeds, it is still paid for even though page two alone satisfies the analysis target.
- Expected: Walk the already-issued bounded provider frontier first. Only if those pages are exhausted and valid inventory is still below the fixed analysis target may Gemini plan zero-result recovery. The recovery plan retains the same search/segmentation ceilings and healthy cursor success makes no extra model call.
- Root cause: Recovery expansion and metadata retention are executed eagerly before `_continue_provider_pages`; query dispatch is lazy, but model planning is not.
- Universal fix and focused retest: `_continue_provider_pages` invokes one lazy recovery factory only after all existing cursor branches exhaust below the target, computing capacity from the then-remaining search budget. A page-two success test uses a recovery stub that would raise and proves it is never called; mixed cursor/recovery and exact-budget controls prove bounded fallback still runs when needed.

### AF-254 — Mixed original-cursor and recovery sources can carry one mismatched response contract

AF-252 through AF-254 pass 15 focused tests, all 274 retrieval tests, and 443 retrieval plus affected ingestion diagnostics; an independent eight-test audit also passes.

### Final local release gate for AF-240 through AF-254

- Status: GO locally; exact-SHA deployment, scoped production reset, and five-domain live replay remain pending.
- Complete backend: 3,161 passed, 1 intentional skip, and 75 subtests passed. The skip is the legacy local Faster Whisper model path; production transcription remains Groq.
- Production pipeline collection excluding that intentionally unused local-Whisper file: 679 passed.
- Frontend: 218 passed. TypeScript validation and the production Next.js build passed.
- Explicit healthy-path latency/call-budget matrix: 17 passed. It covers one-call/no-wait expansion, one concurrent search stage, no healthy recovery planning, cursor-before-recovery, mixed-contract preservation, bounded long fallback, exactly two Pro selector/audit calls with no retry sleep, one organizer call across five domains, and a fresh execution deadline only after durable queue leasing.
- Independent final audits: generation continuation/restatement 7 passed; final recovery/duration/contract audit 9 passed; production files compile and the non-graph diff check is clean. No domain allowlist, lexical topic matcher, extra healthy provider call, larger search/segmentation prefix, or unresolved code blocker remains.
- Required graph refresh: AST extraction completed for all 413 files. The graph tool then reproduced its pre-existing NetworkX betweenness-centrality stall and was interrupted after 90 seconds; generated `graphify-out` files remain outside the release index.
